Current Affairs Commentary

Yugoslavia's Internal Stabilization Movement

— Ang

The reorganization of the Yugoslav cabinet last month was the result of the unexpected success of the anti-government faction in the parliamentary re-election on May 5th. The deeper cause was the assassination of King Alexander on October 9th last year. Ever since the Marseilles Affair shocked the world, Yugoslavia has deeply felt the need for internal political reform. Thus, Wang Fubi, who had always been in a detached position, and Ye Fudi recruited figures from past and present parties to form a mixed cabinet. Now, with Finance Minister Situ Yadi, who sympathizes with the Croats, the so-called "Comfort Cabinet" has been organized. This cannot be said to be a major change in Yugoslavia's internal politics.

Yugoslavia is a newly emerging country after the war. Its domestic ethnic complexity is the highest among the Balkan countries. It currently has approximately 94,000 square miles of land, more than double that of Serbia before the war. The population is approximately 14 million, more than triple that of before the war. Domestic political problems have come with the expansion of national strength. At the beginning of its founding, it was originally based on Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes as the ethnic foundation, and the Corfu Treaty of 1917 as the political foundation, with the common support of the Hella George dynasty to implement a constitutional republic of the three ethnic groups. However, as things changed, the political ideologies of the Serbs and Croats tended to be extreme. The Serbs, with new enemies and old hatreds surrounding them on all sides, believed that they could not survive without centralized unification. The radical party, holding power, gradually became autocratic. The Croats and Slovenes, who were accustomed to German culture, regarded the Slavic culture of the Serbs as superior, and their belief in Roman Catholicism was opposed to the Greek Orthodox religion of the Serbs. Therefore, they were unwilling to be oppressed for a long time. Since the founding of Yugoslavia, the internal politics have been mired in open and secret struggles over the issue of centralization and decentralization, and there has been no peaceful day. During this period, cabinet members were murdered, party leaders were attacked, the Croatian province twice brewed independence, anti-government parties were repeatedly banned, the king personally exercised dictatorship, and the constitution was revised by decree, until the great outbreak of the Marseilles Affair in October last year.

The leader of the Croatian opposition party, Magiak, was imprisoned in January last year for demanding autonomy, but was pardoned after the Marseilles incident. People regarded this as a precursor to Yugoslavia's efforts to win back the people's hearts. When Ye Fudi formed a cabinet, he also issued a declaration of governing the country, advocating the equality of all people and planning to reform administrative agencies to make the provinces autonomous units, striving to implement a system of both centralization and decentralization under a unified government. Recently, the parliament has been re-elected, and all parties that were previously dissolved have been allowed to form new parties to engage in elections. From the surface, it seems that the internal situation has gradually become more compromised. In fact, the fundamental differences between the ethnic groups have not been quietly eliminated. The imperial constitution of 1931 has a provision that political parties must not be organized on the basis of religion or local boundaries, intending to disperse the strength of the opposition, which has been deeply resented by the Croats. Now, not only does this provision still exist, but during the election process, the official did not hesitate to use police force in the Croatian province to arrest a large number of opposition parties. Sixty-seven elected opposition members subsequently agreed not to go to the new parliament at a meeting in Zagreb, the capital of Croatia. When the cabinet tide rose again, the regent summoned the leader of the opposition party, Magiak, to Beijing for consultation. Magiak recommended that the Chief of the Army General Staff, Ye Guowei, organize a neutral cabinet and make the restoration of free elections to complete the constitutional parliament as its mission. Before the discussion was completed, Magiak quietly returned to Zagreb on the day the new cabinet of Situ Yadi was established. Is this not a manifestation that the three ethnic groups cannot fundamentally cooperate?

Although the new prime minister announced the general policy of the government to the parliament yesterday, saying that the government will formulate laws in accordance with public opinion so that the majority of the people can participate in the government, and sincerely requested the whole country to eliminate ethnic prejudices, stop political disputes, and cooperate in seeking the country. Since the new government has made this further expression in this stalemate, the three ethnic groups, which have always been uneasy, may not find it difficult to reorganize and unite under mutual understanding, and the ethnic problems of Yugoslavia may be solved from now on.

Eliminating the East African War: British Active Diplomacy, the Crux of the Situation Lies in France's Attitude, and the King of Abyssinia's Request for Intervention Plunges America into a Predicament; the Kellogg-Briand Pact Faces Another Acid Test

(Paris) Prime Minister Laval held another meeting today with the British Ambassador regarding the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. According to news from diplomatic sources, the British government has already initiated diplomatic actions in various national capitals concerning the Abyssinian issue. (National Telegraph, 4th)

(Paris) Reuters has learned that the focus of the Italian-Abyssinian case has now shifted to Paris. The United Kingdom, as a member of the League of Nations, is cautiously inquiring based on its collective obligations. The UK's policy seems not to evade its obligations, but if other relevant countries refuse to share the burden, the UK does not want to bear the full responsibility alone. It is widely believed that the UK will not invoke Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant to initiate economic sanctions against the aggressor. The UK is currently striving to prevent the outbreak of war in Northeast Africa and is making it clear that it cannot be expected to bear any risks or actions that may arise in the process alone. No action will be taken without prior consultation with the Dominions. One of the issues that needs careful consideration is the possible impact of the Abyssinian war on other parts of Africa. Africans are now closely watching the progress of the dispute negotiations. The French government also attaches great importance to the Abyssinian issue, and its enthusiasm for eliminating war is no less than that of the UK. It is said that France's policy advocates staying away from the League of Nations, as Italy is extremely tense about this matter, and a slight mistake could easily provoke its anger. However, it will still strive to find a solution through direct negotiations. But it must be known now that the time for leisurely discussions is coming to an end. (Reuters, 5th)

It was learned here today in the Abyssinian capital that the Abyssinian government has requested the United States to consider how to force Italy to comply with the Kellogg-Briand Pact. It is reported that this request was submitted to Mr. Henson, the U.S. Chargé d'Affaires here, for transmission to Washington. (National Telegraph, 4th)

(Washington) The State Department stated today that it has received Abyssinia's request for intervention in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, as the United States, Italy, and Abyssinia are all signatories to the Kellogg Pact. According to reports, officials had previously denied receiving this request. Although this announcement has now been made, the authorities are still unwilling to make any comments. (National Telegraph, 4th)

(Washington) According to political circles here today, the King of Abyssinia sent a petition yesterday to the American Chargé d'Affaires in Abyssinia, requesting the United States to invoke the Kellogg-Briand Pact regarding the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. Secretary of State Hull will carefully consider the reply. Well-informed sources feel that this document has placed the United States in a very difficult position. If the reply rejects this request, it will be seen as evading the obligations of the pact. If the United States invokes the pact, it could easily lead to a dispute with Italy. In view of the fact that the previous two times the pact was invoked were ineffective, it is widely believed that the only possible action the United States can take is to announce that the United States does not recognize the annexation of territory by force, as it did in the case of "Manchukuo." (Reuters, 5th)

MacDonald Explains British Foreign Policy: Always Adhering to the Obligations of the League of Nations Covenant, the Cause of Peace Depends on International Cooperation

(London) Lord President MacDonald recently gave a radio broadcast speech, responding to various criticisms from the outside world regarding the government's foreign policy, roughly saying, "The current international situation is difficult to be optimistic about, I know this very well, but the responsibility does not lie solely with the government of one country. The government of one country cannot force the actions of other countries' governments. Those who generally criticize the government's foreign policy often do not examine the facts carefully, as if all countries in the world except the United Kingdom have no freedom of action, and the United Kingdom can force countries like Germany, Italy, and Japan to obey its will, and all peace undertakings can be accomplished solely by us. If that were the case, wouldn't that be absurd? The British government's attitude at the League of Nations meetings and the negotiations in Paris, Rome, and Stresa has been clear. All voters who are willing to help create peace agree with this policy. Our British government's external actions have shown our determination to safeguard peace in more ways than one, and the resolution of the Saar issue is one of the most obvious examples. We have always adhered to the obligations of member states of the League of Nations and recognize that we should cooperate closely with the United States. We have done our best in the past to promote world peace, and we will certainly do our best to do so in the future," and so on. (Havas, 4th)

London Official Circles State That Economic Blockade Is Not Yet Being Discussed

(London) It is widely rumored in Rome and Paris that if Italy insists on going to war with Abyssinia, the UK will take economic blockade measures. However, according to official circles here tonight, this approach is not yet being discussed. (National Telegraph, 5th)

British Members of Parliament Ask Questions One After Another; Eden's Suggestion Arouses Repercussions

(London) Recently, Minister Without Portfolio Eden, when he went to Rome, told Italian Prime Minister Mussolini that the UK was willing to cede a corner of British Somaliland to Abyssinia to provide it with an access to the sea. When the House of Commons met today, members of Parliament asked questions one after another. Colonial Secretary Malcolm MacDonald replied that the land mentioned in Eden's tentative suggestion was the port of Zeila, about fifty miles long and twelve miles wide, adjacent to the Abyssinian border. Its population is about three thousand in the summer and about seven thousand in the winter. The hinterland has no fixed residents, only nomadic tribes visit from time to time. Then Conservative MP Peter MacDonald asked the government that when re-mentioning this tentative suggestion, it should first seriously consider the panic that will arise among the tribesmen in various parts of the Empire, which was warmly welcomed by the entire House. The Colonial Secretary then reiterated that Eden's suggestion was conditional on British tribesmen enjoying water and grass rights on any land ceded by the UK to Italy and Abyssinia. Members continued to ask questions one after another, which was stopped by Speaker FitzRoy. (Reuters, 4th)

Britain Wants to Rely on France; No Longer Opposes Eastern European Pact

(London) According to well-informed sources, if Italy attacks Abyssinia and France assists British action in Geneva, the UK is prepared to consider a compromise with France on the issue of land and air armaments. It is now reported that the UK no longer opposes the conclusion of an Eastern European Pact. However, it is not yet known whether the UK is willing to assume clear obligations to maintain the independence of Austria. (Havas, 4th)

Maintaining the Credibility of the League of Nations: London People's Opinions Are Consistent

(London) The Times commented on the current dispute between Italy and Abyssinia, believing that this case is a "European event and should naturally be resolved through diplomatic channels by the countries concerned in accordance with the principles contained in the League of Nations Covenant." There is no reason to be pessimistic, but the procedure stipulated in the London Declaration of February 3 by the UK and France has become more difficult to implement due to Italy's threat to Abyssinia. Maintaining the credibility of the League of Nations is of course a matter of urgency, but the UK's interests in the border areas of British Kenya, Somaliland, and Sudan in Africa, as well as the UK's position in Egypt, should also be taken into account at the same time. (Havas, 5th)

(London) The Manchester Guardian commented on the British government's policy on the Abyssinian issue, saying that as a member state of the League of Nations, the UK should assume collective obligations, but it has no individual obligations. "As far as the British people are concerned, the UK can only do something if other countries can fulfill the obligations of member states. The British people will not approve of the British government taking unilateral action." Some say that "the key to the situation lies in Paris," which is probably to shift the responsibility for preventing war to France. In fact, regardless of the outcome of the diplomatic strategies of various countries, the Abyssinian issue should still be discussed by the League of Nations. (Havas, 5th)

(London) The League of Nations Association recently held a meeting in Cambridge. After discussing the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, it resolved to urge the cabinet to adopt the most stringent measures to maintain peace and preserve the supreme authority of the League of Nations in handling international disputes. (Havas, 4th)

France's Attitude: Willing to Consider Any Suggestions as Long as They Do Not Hinder Italian-French Friendship

(Paris) British Ambassador Sir Clark visited Prime Minister Laval this afternoon. The British cabinet discussed the Abyssinian issue yesterday, and Clark's meeting with Laval was related to this issue. Diplomats pointed out that France is eager to find a peaceful solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. Prime Minister Laval stated in Geneva that he would be happy to put forward to Italy any suggestion that would resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute as long as it did not harm Italian-French friendship. France's attitude has not changed at present. (Havas, 4th)

(London) The British government is negotiating with France to seek joint British-French action to request economic sanctions from the League of Nations to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. Italian sources here believe that this British negotiation is only a diplomatic means, and the UK's real policy is not in this. British public opinion has recently been advocating the maintenance of the authority of the League of Nations, and the British cabinet's attitude is mostly influenced by this public opinion. Italian sources also believe that France will certainly not agree to adopt an unfriendly policy towards Italy. The UK's actions are at most to show public opinion that the British government has done its best to maintain peace. Even if the UK blockades the Suez Canal, Italy will not find it difficult to find foreign ships to transport Italian troops and military supplies to East Africa. (Havas, 4th)

Italy and France Have a Military Alliance

(London) Several morning newspapers today published articles about the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, saying that France may not agree to apply sanctions to Italy because France recently signed a treaty with Italy, with an agreement attached, allowing Italy freedom of action in Abyssinia and stating that France has no interest in Abyssinia outside the railway area. This Franco-Italian agreement is essentially a military alliance, allowing the Franco-Italian general staff to greatly reduce their border defenses. Therefore, the military strength on the Franco-Italian border is very weak, and Italian troops can freely be transferred to Africa. (Reuters, 5th)

French Island in the Red Sea Ceded to Italy

(Paris) According to British newspapers, the French government ceded the French island of Doumeira in the Red Sea to Italy. The island is located at the border between French Somaliland and Italian Eritrea. Recently, French Chief of Staff General Gamelin ceded the island to Italy during his visit to Rome. According to French officials, the island was ceded to Italy on January 7 this year and has nothing to do with the colonial agreement in the Franco-Italian agreement or the recent arms talks between the two countries. (Havas, 5th)

French Newspapers Ridicule Britain's Contradictory Policy

(Paris) French newspapers are now criticizing Britain's attitude towards the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, saying that Britain was unwilling to use the League of Nations Covenant to sanction Germany, but now it suddenly wants to invoke the Covenant for the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. Why is it so contradictory? Le Petit Parisien published an article by Pierre Berthé, saying that Britain is appealing to the League of Nations for an event that concerns the life and death of the League of Nations, its purpose is to defend the borders of Africa, not the borders of Europe. If France unwisely joins this undertaking, Italy will cite Hitler as a comrade. L'Oeuvre, a newspaper of the Radical Socialist Party, said that Britain's support for the League of Nations Covenant and sanctions is surprising, because not long ago, Britain signed the Anglo-German Naval Agreement and undermined the Treaty of Versailles. The newspaper also said that French Prime Minister Laval will certainly not abandon Italy. (Reuters, 5th)

Arbitration Committee Meeting: Listening to the Defense of the Italian Representative

The Permanent Arbitration Committee on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute met yesterday in The Hague and heard the defense of Italian representative Professor Le Sasha Nai. Le asked the committee to specify the date, time, and location for the Italian side to summon native witnesses who had witnessed or heard about the Walwal incident to attend the meeting and describe the situation at that time. All witnesses will be flown to a designated location in Southern Europe. Members of the arbitration committee will go there to listen to the testimony and then return to Scheveningen to continue the meeting. (Havas, 4th)

Italian Newspapers Denounce Britain

(Rome) After two weeks of silence, Italian newspapers today resumed their attacks on Britain. An editorial in "Il Giornale d'Italia" stated that Britain is carrying out propaganda on both the economic and political fronts in order to completely occupy Abyssinia. It is generally believed that since there are so many anti-British comments, Prime Minister Mussolini's order prohibiting Italian newspapers from attacking Britain has probably been lifted. (National Telegraph, 4th)

(Rome) Italian newspapers today published comments again, criticizing Britain's attitude towards the Abyssinian issue. Corriere della Sera said, "Does Britain really want to uphold justice and fairness? Britain has been planning to manage Abyssinia for more than a day. At first, it tried to monopolize the water conservancy of Lake Tana, and then it established British trading bases in the Gambella area of Abyssinia, even setting up customs to collect taxes and building roads to monopolize the right to exploit the platinum mines in the area. Initially, a British financial group established the Abyssinian Silver Company, which led to the Abyssinian financial turmoil in 1929. Currently, the British are setting up a real estate company in Abyssinia in order to monopolize the development rights of the land around Lake Tana. Abyssinia has resisted the intrusion of foreign forces in every possible way. Later, the British government promised to give the Abyssinian government various concessions and allowed it to assist in Abyssinia's national defense. The establishment of this company was only accepted by the Abyssinian government. From this, it is not difficult to see Britain's intentions in maintaining justice." (Havas, 4th)

(Rome) The local public opinion has been concerned about the issue of Britain's plan to use economic sanctions against Italy through the League of Nations when conflicts occur between Italy and Abyssinia in the future. The Il Popolo di Roma stated, "This is a threat to Italy from the UK and it will be very difficult to turn it into a reality." Il Giornale d'Italia stated, "Economic blockade cannot be implemented without the use of force. The UK's use of the League of Nations as a shield is only to set up a barrier for its own interests in order to cover up the gradual monopolization of Abyssinian territory. This monopolization action has already begun." Il Messaggero, after elaborating on Britain's various activities in Abyssinia, issued the conclusion that "Britain's ambition for Abyssinia was suddenly exposed and greatly hindered by Italy's actions. The world should know that the financial assistance that Britain gave to Abyssinia has been accepted by Abyssinia and used for military expenditures." (Havas, 5th)

Results of Berlin Talks: Germany and Poland Maintain Friendly Relations, Review of General European Issues, Both Sides Largely Agree

(Berlin) After Germany and Poland announced their friendship last year, the situation in Eastern Europe stabilized. Now, in order to further enhance friendship, Polish Foreign Minister Beck came to Berlin at the invitation of the German government. Today, he met with German Head of State Hitler. This is the first meeting between the leaders of the two countries since the adoption of a friendly policy. It is expected that Poland feels somewhat uneasy about the impact of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement and wants to obtain assurances regarding the impact of this agreement on Germany's Baltic policy. After four hours of talks with Hitler, Beck issued a statement saying that the problem was discussed peacefully during the meeting, and other events related to the overall European situation, such as the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance agreement, etc. Beck said that the talk was an active contribution to the 1934 declaration. Last year's declaration has become an element of maintaining peace. The German government's bulletin said that the two sides conducted talks in an open spirit and agreed on many points. (Reuters, 4th)

Public Communique As Usual

(Berlin) The official statement released last night said that Polish Foreign Minister Beck stayed here for two days so that Prime Minister Hitler and German government officials could have the opportunity to discuss issues related to the two countries of Germany and Poland and general European policies in good faith. On the whole, the opinions of the two sides have been unified. It is also determined that the German-Polish Declaration of January 26, 1934, is not only conducive to the mutual relations between the two countries, but also an advisory element for maintaining European peace, and we are greatly honored. Foreign Minister Beck solemnly stated that Prime Minister Hitler's declaration on Poland on May 21 and his expectations for the permanent and unchanging German-Polish agreement have resonated with the Polish side. Poland also hopes that the good neighborly relations with Germany will improve day by day. The two governments know that the two countries are adjacent to each other and will continue to maintain close relations and do their best to promote peace in Europe. (National Telegraph, 4th)

The Scope of Understanding Between the Two Countries

(Berlin) When Polish Minister Beck talked with Head of State Hitler, it did not seem to plan for any hostile plans for any country, especially for the Soviet Union and France. Regarding the two issues of the Free City of Danzig and the Polish Corridor, Colonel Beck did not make clear statements. According to Polish sources, Poland still insists on maintaining the status quo for the existing borders in Europe and is unwilling to change them. As for Germany's rearmament, since it has been recognized by the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, Polish people are extremely uneasy about it. Colonel Beck was heard to have asked Head of State Hitler for assurances that the freedom of maritime traffic must be maintained under any circumstances. In that case, it is not difficult to infer the true scope of the understanding between Germany and Poland, that is, the existing outstanding cases of permanence between the two countries will not be damaged by these talks. As a result of the talks, only an agreement was reached to jointly seek a peaceful solution to the problem. (Havas, 5th)

Paris Pays Close Attention

(Paris) Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck's conversations with German Head of State Hitler have been kept secret. Newspapers are paying attention to them. "Le Journal" protested because Colonel Beck refused to meet with reporters from French newspapers, saying that "Colonel Beck's declaration to German reporters was quite vague and elusive. Therefore, the nature of the meeting between Beck and Hitler should not be exaggerated, but neither can it be underestimated." Le Matin said, "Although there were no concrete results from the talks, from the perspective of Poland's position, Colonel Beck's achievements on this trip should be important." L'Excelsior reported that "Beck's declaration was profound and, according to the impression of diplomats, was aimed at France." Famous political commentator Domeison published an article in Le Figaro commenting on the issue of treaty revision, saying, "Although the Third Reich now sees the German-Polish alliance as beneficial to it, it is not known how long it will last." (Havas, 5th)

The Polish Press Expresses Gratification

Warsaw The Polish newspapers were satisfied with the Berlin side's warm welcome to Foreign Minister Beck. Most said that the Polish Foreign Minister's visit to Berlin was the first time since the eighteenth century, which shows that this move is indeed a proof of the emergence of a new era in Eastern Europe. The newspapers are especially pleased that Hitler personally responded to Beck's banquet. The Polish Daily newspaper stated in its editorial that the results of Foreign Minister's journey have fully proved that the good relationship created by the German-Polish non-aggression treaty has increased unabated, and there is absolutely no pessimism component. Polish express news said that the excellent treatment received by the Polish Foreign Minister in Pahlin this time may not have been such a gratifying result two years ago. Another military agency's newspaper stated that Beck's mission is not only extremely important for German-Polish relations, but also has a great impact on the European situation as a whole. Judging from the announcements published by the German newspaper, it can be seen that the purpose of Beck's trip has been fully achieved. Another newspaper believes that the views of the two countries have become more harmonious and consistent through this exchange. (National Telegraph, 5th)

Commemorating the Fallen Soldiers

(Berlin) Polish Foreign Minister Beck continued to exchange views with Foreign Minister Neurath yesterday. Mr. Beck then visited the Berlin Memorial Hall for Fallen Soldiers of the European War. Army Chief of Staff Blumberg, German Army Commander-in-Chief Fritsch, and other senior officials were all present to welcome him. After accepting the salute of the guards, Mr. Beck entered the memorial hall to lay a wreath and stood in silence for several minutes to commemorate the fallen soldiers of the European War. Yesterday, Polish Ambassador Lipski held a banquet. Prime Minister Hitler went to the embassy to thank the Polish Foreign Minister and also attended. The crowd in front of the embassy was cheering loudly. (National Telegraph, 4th)

The Soviet Russian Navy Changes to Display a New Flag

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian Navy will henceforth display a new naval flag stipulated by the Central Executive Committee. Its style is a white background with a blue border below, with a five-pointed star in the middle and a hammer and sickle valley one. After this flag is used, the current red flag will be abolished. The Soviet Union Again Expresses Approval to Japan for the Establishment of a Border Joint Committee; The Russian Ambassador and the Japanese Foreign Minister Talk for Two Hours; and Hope That Japan Will Study Specific Plans; Japan Believes That the Invasion of Russian Territory Is Not a Fact

(Nanjing) Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev visited Foreign Minister Hirota at the Foreign Ministry at 3:20 pm on the 5th and reached two and a half hours. He held important consultations on the issue of protesting the so-called border crossing incident proposed by the Soviet Union and the establishment of a joint committee on the border between Manchuria and the Soviet Union. It is said that during the meeting, Ambassador Yurenev, according to the reply from his country's government, said that during the meeting between Hirota and Yurenev on the 26th of last month, Foreign Minister Hirota proposed the establishment of a committee to handle disputes on the border between Manchuria and the Soviet Union. The Soviet government replied that it recognized this proposal, but the future negotiation methods and its specific plan should be fully considered by the Soviet government, and it is hoped that Japan will also study it. Foreign Minister Hirota immediately notified "Manchukuo" of this understanding of the Soviet government's approval of the establishment of a border committee. Regarding the negotiation method, it must be fully agreed upon, and it has been replied in this way. The meeting on the 5th did not mention the start time and location of negotiations on the establishment of a border committee. However, after the three countries of Japan, Manchuria, and the Soviet Union fully agree on the above negotiation method, it is planned to start negotiations as soon as possible. The steps are roughly like this. As for Ambassador Yurenev's meeting on the 5th, he did not touch on the so-called issue of Japanese troops crossing the border that was raised by the Soviet Union. The previous telegram was wrong, so I would like to make a note of it. (Nichi-Rengo, 5th)

(Tokyo) Ambassador to Manchuria Minami Jiro reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 5th that after Japanese and Manchurian officials received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, they tried their best to investigate the truth about the border crossing incident by Japanese and Manchurian troops. However, as the Soviet government protested, such as Japanese and Manchurian soldiers crossing the border and warships invading Russia, etc., are not true. It is difficult to understand why the Soviet Union deliberately publicizes this kind of incident and protests to the Japanese government. Or it may be that the situation is favorable for the establishment of a joint border committee. (Nichi-Rengo, 5th)

Large-Scale Air Defense Exercise in Japan

To be held simultaneously in Tokyo, Kawasaki, and Yokohama from this morning until tomorrow morning.

(Tokyo) From the 6th to the 7th, Tokyo, Kawasaki, and Yokohama will hold air defense exercises. Approximately 350,000 personnel from the three cities' defense corps will participate. In addition, numerous special defense corps from large stores, factories, temples, and women's groups will also participate. The exercise will begin around 11:00 AM on the 6th, simulating a scenario where several dozen aircraft from a certain country, loaded with incendiary bombs, attack Tokyo with the aim of bombing it. The defense corps will begin operations based on this scenario. Each district defense group will reinforce its designated area by 2:00 PM, aiming to completely defend Tokyo against dozens of simulated enemy aircraft. From 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM, these aircraft will be detected over the three cities, attempting to bomb the congested area around Shinjuku Station. The defense corps headquarters and district defense personnel will strive to rescue, provide fire protection, and evacuate from fires and injuries caused by the aircraft's bombing. At night, more than forty enemy aircraft, divided into over ten teams, will attack, dropping incendiary bombs everywhere. Citizens will completely enter alert and control until sunset. During each air raid, strict control measures will be implemented, plunging Tokyo into darkness to provide cover. Anti-aircraft guns and machine gun emplacements will be set up everywhere to repel the enemy aircraft. At dawn on the 7th, enemy aircraft will engage in a dawn battle with ground troops. During the blackout on the night of the 6th, no light will be allowed to leak from railways or any transportation facilities. These measures will be implemented, with vehicles operating in the darkened city, creating a realistic combat situation. As a result, Tokyo was already bustling with preparations for the air defense exercise on the 5th. (Jiji News Agency, 5th)

British Air Force Budget: Additional £5 Million

To be submitted to the House of Commons next week.

(London) The Cabinet has decided to submit a proposal to the House of Commons next week for an additional £5 million to the Air Force budget. This additional budget is intended to supplement Air Force equipment and pay Air Force salaries before the end of the current fiscal year on March 31, 1936. It is also reported that the Home Office will issue a notice to local authorities within days regarding their responsibilities for taking precautionary measures in the event of an air raid, urging them to focus on training and organize lectures to educate the public about air defense. However, all proposed measures are not mandatory for the public to follow. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

Wording similar to France; Acknowledges that the Franco-Soviet Pact does not conflict with the Locarno Treaty.

(London) Germany had inquired with the British government whether the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance treaty conflicted with the Locarno Treaty. The British government has today sent a reply to the German ambassador, with wording similar to France, stating that it does not conflict. A Reuters diplomatic correspondent learned that London now feels the overall situation is stabilizing, as Germany is about to initiate the organization of Eastern European security. (Reuters News Agency, 5th)

Italian Diplomatic Reshuffle

(Rome) A large-scale reshuffle of Italian ambassadors has recently taken place. The current Italian Ambassador to Russia, Attolico, has been reassigned as Ambassador to Germany. The current Ambassador to Germany, Cerruti, has been reassigned as Ambassador to France. The current Ambassador to France, Count De Gusto Chabot, has been reassigned as Ambassador to the Vatican. Key Austrian Figures Travel to Italy and Hungary; Restoration Movement Takes Another Step

(Vienna) Today, the Parliament has approved the government's decision to repeal the law exiling the Habsburg royal family and return their former assets. This is another step in Austria's move towards restoration. Simultaneously, Vice-Chancellor and leader of the Home Guard, Prince Starhemberg, flew to Rome today, widely believed to be to consult with Italian leader Mussolini regarding the recent developments concerning a possible Habsburg restoration. Furthermore, Defense Minister Vaugoins also flew to Budapest, the capital of Hungary, today, reportedly to meet with leaders of the Hungarian legitimist movement. (Reuters News Agency, 4th)

(Vienna) The State Council's passage of the law repealing measures against the Habsburg royal family has caused a great stir in political circles here. It is now understood that the bill not only stipulates the restoration of the royal family's private property, but also, in principle, acknowledges the Habsburg royal family's right to return to the country. The Secretary-General of the State Council, Gawainski, along with several financial experts, is currently negotiating with representatives of the royal family residing in Belgium. The heir to the Austro-Hungarian throne, Archduke Otto, has been informed of the government's intentions. There is much discussion about the impact of Archduke Otto and Empress Zita's return on the political situation. Everyone is wondering when their return will take place. Well-informed sources believe it will be in the autumn. (National News Agency, 4th)

(Vienna) The bill is currently being discussed by the Economic Council established under the January 1934 constitution. The amendments to the bill regarding the status of the Habsburg royal family are mainly in two areas: (1) Currently, members of the royal family traveling abroad must change their names. In the future, they can be issued Austrian government passports by Austrian authorities. (2) The state will provide the royal family with living expenses, even when residing abroad. However, the government currently does not favor any member of the royal family residing in Austria for a long time, and monarchists also do not advocate for immediate restoration to avoid international difficulties for the government. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

(Vienna) Archduke Otto declared in Belgium that he would not return to Vienna unless he could ascend the throne. However, this point is still uncertain. (National News Agency, 4th)

Foreign Minister's Statement: (Vienna) After the State Council meeting, Foreign Minister Weidigg explained that the bill has nothing to do with restoration. "I believe the issue of restoration is not yet timely. The Austrian government has always adopted an honest and transparent approach. Austria will not take any steps that could cause disputes in Europe. This should be trusted by foreign countries. Therefore, foreign countries should not object to the bill presented today," he said. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

Reactions from Various Countries: (Paris) The repeal of the law exiling the Habsburg royal family, requested by the Austrian government, is considered inopportune by the local newspapers. Le Petit Parisien reported, "Under the current situation in Europe, the Austrian government should have avoided such a move, as Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia will see this as a prelude to the restoration of the Habsburg royal family. This is a pretext for war that the Little Entente countries can invoke." L'Écho de Paris believes that the situation in Central Europe may become complicated. Le Populaire, the Socialist newspaper, stated, "If the Austrian government's move is used as a pretext for restoration in the near future, it will inevitably lead to a serious crisis of war." The Communist Party's organ "L'Humanité" said that the Austrian government's move is a threat to peace. Le Journal published a statement by Weissner, the leader of the Austrian monarchists, stating, "The only way to stabilize the situation in Austria and maintain its independence is to restore the traditional monarchy. The successors of the Austro-Hungarian Empire need not doubt the Habsburg royal family's return to the throne, as this is the only way to prevent the development of Pan-Germanism." L'Excelsior said, "Austria cannot survive independently of its neighboring countries and should not offend them, which Austria deeply knows. Austria is courageous and courteous, and has no provocative behavior towards any country." (Havas News Agency, 5th)

(Paris) The Yugoslav ambassador to France, Spalajković, visited Premier and Foreign Minister Laval this morning, reportedly to discuss Austria's repeal of the order exiling the Habsburg royal family. According to responsible sources, Laval made a statement on March 15 to the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Senate, stating that the French government's policy on the restoration of the Habsburg royal family is completely the same as that of the Little Entente countries. France's attitude has not changed to this day, but it believes that the measures taken by Austria this time are only related to Austria's internal affairs, so there is no need to take any diplomatic steps. It is regrettable that Austria has taken such measures under the current circumstances, as it is feared that this will cause disputes in Central Europe and hinder the signing of the Danube Pact. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

(Rome) Regarding the issue of the Habsburg royal family's restoration in Austria, Italy does not object, but because this matter may cause a backlash from the Little Entente countries, and to achieve the success of the Danube Conference, Italy must reach an agreement with the Little Entente. Therefore, Italy is currently taking a cautious stance. It is rumored that Austrian Vice-Chancellor Starhemberg is on his way to Italy. According to official statements, it has become a tradition for Starhemberg to come to Italy every year to inspect the Austrian youth summer training camp. This visit was not arranged in advance and has nothing to do with the Habsburg restoration issue. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

Prague: Regarding the Austrian government's request to amend the law exiling the Habsburg royal family, responsible sources in the Czech government believe that it will not affect the Austrian political system. However, if this matter leads to the issue of restoration, the Little Entente countries will have a strong reaction. According to indirect sources, Empress Zita, the former queen of Austria, and Archduke Otto, the heir to the throne, have not benefited from the government's bill. As for the returned property, it is only privately owned by the royal family, and the former royal property is not included. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

Belgrade: Yugoslav political figures believe that the Austrian government's proposal to amend the law exiling the Habsburg royal family is the first step in Austria's preparation for restoration, and they express surprise and unease. (Havas News Agency, 4th)

The Demise of a Royal Grandson: (Berlin) After the Austrian government abolished the law against the Habsburg royal family, there was hope for the royal family to rise again. However, Archduke Ferdinand, a key figure in the royal family, unfortunately passed away here today at the age of 66. His later years were very bleak. Thirty years ago, he renounced his title and became a commoner, changing his name to Hoferlin. He initially served as a colonel in the Austrian army. In 1902, he fell in love with a young actress and wanted to marry her, so he resolutely renounced his hereditary rights and title, changing his name to Hoferlin. He then left Austria and returned to Switzerland. In 1907, he divorced his wife. Soon after, he fell out with the royal family. Not only was his throne not guaranteed, but all of his royal private property was confiscated by the government. As a result, he became extremely poor. In order to make a living, he later worked as a cafe waiter, journalist, insurance salesman, shop assistant, etc. He wandered from Switzerland to Berlin to Vienna, leading a nomadic life. Eventually, he returned to Berlin. Several years later, he married another woman. In addition to several books, his writings mainly consisted of short pieces about the Viennese royal family. (National News Agency, 4th)

Former Spanish King Injured in Car Accident

(Rome) The car carrying former Spanish King Alfonso crashed in Fotonica, causing minor injuries to the former king. The Duke of Miranda, the former king's aide-de-camp, suffered a broken neck and serious injuries. (Havas News Agency, 5th)

Japanese Foreign Minister Reports on "New Life" Incident at Cabinet Meeting

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota reported at the cabinet meeting on the 5th that Ambassador Arima is negotiating with the Chinese authorities regarding the disrespectful incident involving the Chinese magazine "New Life Weekly." The Chinese authorities are expected to accept the Japanese demands. (Jiji News Agency, 5th)

American Independence Day: 91 Deaths Nationwide

(New York) Yesterday was American Independence Day, and 91 people died in accidents across the country, 86 fewer than last year. Due to the ban on the sale of fireworks, only two people died from fireworks, but hundreds were still injured by fireworks. Fourteen people were injured in Washington. (Reuters News Agency, 5th)

International Commercial Telegram

Reuters Commodity Market Report, July 5th

Gold and Silver: British Gold - London gold bonds remained unchanged today at 140 shillings and 11 pence.

British Silver - The London silver market was stable. The current spot price is 31 pence, and the forward price is 31 pence and 1/875, both unchanged. China both bought and sold.

American Silver - The Mountly silver market, futures remained loose. The opening price for September contracts today was 30 points lower than the last closing price, and some were 15 higher.

Exchange Rates: British-American - The London foreign exchange market saw continuous demand for the British pound from Europe. The opening exchange rate for the British pound against the US dollar was $4.94375, up one cent from yesterday's closing price. It fell by 0.0625 after the first hour to $4.943125. Although there were fluctuations, this price remained unchanged until 2:00 PM.

British-French - The opening price remained unchanged at 74.75 francs. It rose by one point in the first hour and continued to rise by nine points at noon, then fell by six points to 74.79 francs. There were no changes until 2:00 PM in the afternoon.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton - The New York cotton market opened sharply lower. The October contract price was 11.62 cents, down 16 points, and then there was a tendency to turn firm.

British Cotton - The Liverpool cotton market was looser today. The October contract price fell 3 points at 1:00 PM to 6.23.

Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was relatively stable today. At 1:00 PM, the October contract price was 4 shillings and 11.5 pence, up half a penny.

American Wheat - The prices of Chicago wheat and grains plummeted today. The September wheat price fell 2.375 to 84.5, and the September grain price also fell 1.125 to 74. The market situation in the morning was uneven and there was no fixed trend. According to London news, there is talk that the Canadian government has changed its food policy. This is the reason for the sharp drop in wheat prices. It is heard that Canada intends to compete in the open market in order to force competitors into international coordination. According to reliable sources, the Canadian government may not immediately reduce wheat prices significantly.

Rubber: London - The London rubber market was stable, but trading later became quiet. The price of October and December contracts at noon was 6.0625 pence, down 0.0625 from yesterday's closing price.

New York - New York rubber opened lower, about 9 points lower than the previous closing price. Trading was sluggish, and merchants wanted to wait for new developments.

Securities: New York - New York securities opened sluggishly, but prices showed a strong trend. The general trend in the morning was upward. Utility stocks were stable, and steel stocks showed some improvement. The average price of the Dow Jones 30 industrial stocks was 118.96, up 15 points. The prices are as follows:

The Big Name Secret Society Incident is Resolved Through Mediation; Peaceful Resolution Expected

(Tianjin) The Jin Shengdao incident in Daming is expected to be resolved peacefully through mediation. Zhao Dehuai, the leader of the secret society, has released Qiu Rugang, the head of the Weixian Collective Civil Defense Corps, and the heads of the four public security sub-bureaus in Jintanji and other areas. However, transportation in Xingtai, Daming, Jize, and Quxian remains disrupted, and telephone and telegraph lines have not been restored. Two commissioners sent by the Hebei Provincial Government returned to Baoding early on the 3rd after consulting with Cheng Tingheng, the magistrate of Daming County, and Guo Xipeng, the commander of the 4th Cavalry Division stationed in the area. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Tianjin) Guo Xipeng, the commander of the 4th Cavalry Division stationed in Daming, issued four warnings to Jin Shengs: 1. Zhao Dehuai and other leaders of the secret society will not be prosecuted for their past actions, so that they can rehabilitate themselves. 2. The leaders of the Jin Shengdao who were arrested will be transferred to the newly established court in Daming for review. 3. At the request of the members of the society, Zhao Dehuai will be given 3,000 yuan in cash to disband the members. 4. The guns and ammunition seized from the various teams and police stations must be returned immediately. If these conditions are met, the siege of the city will be lifted and a solution will be sought. Otherwise, for the sake of protecting the local area, a military attack will be launched. Zhao has softened and is willing to accept. On the 3rd, a large group of bandits, well-equipped with firearms, crossed the border between Hebei and Henan and arrived at Sixth Shop, only 20 li southwest of Daming. Upon hearing the report, Commander Guo Xipeng dispatched troops to meet them. It is reported that this group of bandits is the remnant of Ren Yingqi and Liu Guitang, numbering about 300. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Bai Jianwu Arrives in Dalian

(Beiping) After his defeat, Bai Jianwu fled to Tianjin and hid in a certain concession. He arrived in Dalian on the 4th. The Dalian authorities will monitor him. It is rumored that some of the bandits who mutinied in Changping this time were formerly under Bai's command. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Japanese Side Actively Proceeding with Development of North China's Industries

(Beiping) The Japanese side is actively proceeding with the establishment of the Sino-Japanese joint venture North China Industrial Development Company. Takahashi Kameichi, a consultant to the Japanese Kwantung Army, Yokoyama Minoru, a Japanese financial expert, and Enoube, the Director-General of the Japanese Ministry of Finance, arrived in Dalian from Japan earlier and discussed everything with Doihara, who was staying there. It is reported that a decision has been made regarding the investment portion, and the contents of the company's establishment plan have been largely agreed upon as follows: (1) Sino-Japanese joint venture to develop North China's mineral resources, develop transportation, and promote cotton planting. (2) Establish various Sino-Japanese joint venture industrial companies in major cities in North China, based on the joint venture company. (3) Establish a large-scale financial institution in Tianjin to welcome Chinese capital. The Japanese Ministry of Colonial Affairs and the South Manchuria Railway can also join in the capital. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Smuggling of Silver by Koreans Reduced in Beiping and Tianjin

(Beiping) The smuggling of cash out of Beiping has recently decreased due to effective prevention measures. At the request of our side, the police department of the Japanese Embassy in Beiping has not only dispatched plainclothes police to assist in intercepting smugglers at the railway station, but has also recently sent personnel to wait at banks such as the Bank of China to prevent Koreans from exchanging cash. According to transportation circles, the Japanese side has intercepted many cases of Koreans smuggling silver at the Beiping and Tianjin stations of the Beining Railway in recent months, which has reduced the smuggling of silver by Koreans. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Dismissal of Miners and Staff at Liujiang Coal Mine

(Tianjin) The dispute between the Yuguan Liujiang Coal Mine and Taike over the boundary of the mining area has not been resolved, and negotiations have stalled. Liujiang has repeatedly tried to break the deadlock, but has been unable to do so. The Liujiang Wharf and Warehouse in Qinhuangdao have been sealed for five weeks, causing heavy losses to the company. Zheng Songhua and Fang Zhiwu, the persons in charge of Liujiang, returned from Shanghai on the 4th and will implement the plan decided by the shareholders' meeting held in Shanghai. Except for 20 radio operators, the remaining miners and staff will be given one month's salary and dismissed starting this month. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Japanese Troops in Tianjin Conduct Inspection

(Tianjin) At 11:00 AM on the 5th, Japanese troops in Tianjin conducted an inspection on Miyajima Street and Kasuga Street in the Japanese concession, commanded by Major Mutō, with two companies of infantry and artillery participating. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Tianjin) More than 100 Japanese troops stationed in Tianjin, fully armed, departed from the Haiguangsi barracks at around 1:00 PM on the 5th and paraded along Dongma Road over the Jingang Bridge to the Hebei area, returning to the camp at around 5:00 PM. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Bandit Leader in Longyan Surrenders

(Xiamen) Chen Jincai and two others, the Chairman of the pseudo-Longyan County Soviet, surrendered to the county government with three Mauser pistols. In addition, Lin Wenyan, the director of anti-revolutionary suppression in the pseudo-urban area, also surrendered with two pistols. In recent days, they have led the Suiqu District Headquarters to uncover several pseudo-organs and arrest Liu Jiarong, the Chairman of the pseudo-urban area Soviet. Our army surrounded and captured more than 20 male and female Red bandits near Tianzidong in Jinfeng, Yongding, along with more than 20 rifles, and seized many sewing kits and documents from the pseudo-Min Southwest Guerrilla Department and the Jinfeng District Soviet Government. (Central News Agency, 5th)

Minister of Personnel Affairs, Lin Xiang, Dies in Beijing

(Nanjing) Lin Xiang suffered from cerebral hemorrhage and was treated at the Central Hospital from the 1st. By 2:00 AM on the 4th, his condition had worsened. Upon seeing this, Lin's family moved him back to his residence in Zenggongci, Beijing, overnight. At that time, Lin's temperature was even higher, reaching 39.5 degrees. He passed away at his residence in Beijing at 8:30 AM on the 5th. Lin had six sons and three daughters, who were all by his side and personally helped with the funeral arrangements. Lin was 54 years old, a native of Minhou, and graduated from Meiji University in Japan. He served as the Minister of Justice of the Guangdong Revolutionary Government, the President of the Supreme Court of the National Government, and the current Minister of Personnel Affairs. Upon hearing the news, Dai Chuanxian drove from Tangshan to Lin's residence in the morning of the 5th to offer his condolences, and said that Lin had died of overwork and would immediately submit a request to the government for posthumous commendation. Lin's remains were scheduled to be placed in a coffin at 10:00 PM on the 5th. (Central News Agency, 5th)

Chen Ce Holds Meeting with Captains of Haiqi and Haishen in Hong Kong

(Hong Kong) Chen Ce inspected the Haiqi and Haishen this morning. The Hong Kong naval commander visited the Haiqi. Chen scheduled a return visit for the 6th. Chen held a meeting with the captains of the two ships on the Haiqi, announced the central government's intentions, and all expressed obedience. After replenishing coal and water, they will return north within three or two days. Chen said that his mission was to lead the two ships back north, and he knew nothing else. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Hong Kong) Chen Ce visited the Hong Kong authorities at 9:00 AM on the 5th to thank them for their hospitality towards the two ships. (Central News Agency, 5th)

China National Aviation Corporation Increases Flights on the Hankou-Chongqing Route

(Nanjing) The China National Aviation Corporation's Sichuan route flies in three sections: Shanghai-Hankou, Hankou-Chongqing, and Chongqing-Chengdu. Now, according to an order from the Ministry of Communications, one additional round-trip flight will be added on the Hankou-Chongqing section, which will be implemented from the 1st of this month. After the assembly of new aircraft is completed, it is also planned to change all flights on the Hankou-Chongqing and Chongqing-Chengdu sections to daily round-trip flights. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has submitted a proposal to the government for controlling import trade and managing international exchange rates. According to responsible officials of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, this proposal is an effective method for balancing international trade and will be discussed in detail with the Ministry of Finance. However, the method of consultation, whether it will be convened by the Executive Yuan or directly consulted with the Ministry of Finance by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, has not yet been determined. (Central News Agency, 5th)

Disciplinary Actions for Dereliction of Duty in Henan

(Nanjing) Yao Jiawang, the Magistrate of Fengqiu County in Henan, Zhang Xiezhong, the District Head, Liu Hao, Hu Yuzhang, and Li Zanlong, Judges of the Bian District Court, were impeached by Supervisor Du Chen of the Control Yuan for a case of dereliction of duty, harming the people, perverting the law, and showing partiality. After deliberation by the Central Disciplinary Committee, it was decided that Yao's monthly salary be reduced by 10% for a period of three months, Zhang be demoted one grade and reassigned, and Liu, Hu, and Li each receive a written reprimand. Furthermore, Yin Chunrong, the Deputy Squad Leader of the Henan Salt Affairs Tax Police, was also impeached for a case of brutalizing the people, and the Central Disciplinary Committee decided to dismiss him from his post and suspend him from employment for one year. (Central News Agency dispatch, 5th)

Central Government Sends Personnel to Estimate the Renovation of the Confucius Temple in Qufu

(Nanjing) Tang Wencong and Zhong Lingxiu returned to Beijing after going to Shandong to estimate the cost of renovating the Confucius Temple. Tang stated that the estimated budget for the renovation of the Confucius Temple is over 1.1 million yuan. The original plan by the Shandong Construction Department required 890,000 yuan. Now, after re-evaluation, the Confucius Temple section requires approximately 800,000 yuan plus some additional expenses. Outside of the Confucius Temple, the attached areas, such as the renovation of the Yan Temple (estimated at over 40,000 yuan), the road surface from the Confucius Temple to the Confucius Forest (estimated at tens of thousands of yuan), and the road from Yanzhou to Qufu (estimated at over 80,000 yuan), are necessary to renovate at the same time, as these places are essential routes for Chinese and foreign visitors to the Confucius Temple. Furthermore, 100,000 yuan is needed for the workers' pay, and 50,000 yuan is tentatively set aside for design and supervision fees over two years, totaling approximately 1.1 million yuan. The Central Government previously discussed allocating 200,000 yuan, with the remainder to be apportioned among the provinces according to the same ratio used for the construction of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum. The date of commencement will be determined after the Executive Yuan approves the budget. (Special dispatch, 5th)

Municipal Conference in Beijing Passes the Reorganization of the Land Office

(Nanjing) At the municipal conference held by the Beijing Municipal Government on the 5th, the decision was made to reorganize the Land Office into the Land Bureau. The matter was handed over to the Counselor's Office to draft organizational regulations, which will then be submitted to the Mayor for referral to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation. (Special dispatch, 5th)

National Government Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics Plans to Convene a National Statistics Conference

(Nanjing) According to reports from various provinces to the Statistics Bureau of the National Government's Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, 18 provinces, municipalities, and districts have established statistical organizations. However, all feel that the forms issued by various central government agencies are numerous and repetitive, making them difficult to fill out. Tax-Exempt Passports for Foreign Rice Are Sold at a Discount by Officials and Merchants

(Nanjing) Citizens such as Xu Yisai submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance stating that some officials and gentry who had obtained tax-exempt passports to import foreign rice were not actually selling the rice at a fair price. Instead, they were privately selling the passports to rice merchants in Shanghai, Wuhu, and other places at a discount based on the amount of rice tax. They also provided a copy and serial number of a passport obtained in Liu'an, requesting that the Jianghai Customs and other customs offices be instructed to detain any such passports encountered. The Ministry of Finance stated that if the reported circumstances were true, it would betray the government's intention to provide disaster relief to the people. It immediately instructed the provincial governments to conduct a thorough investigation. At the same time, it ordered all customs offices to detain Liuhe passports for investigation and to serve as a warning. (Special dispatch, 5th)

Salt Transport Commissioner of Changlu Drafts Measures to Rectify Nitre Salt in Hebei Province

(Nanjing) The Changlu Salt Transport Commissioner, in light of the widespread use of nitre salt in Hebei, drafted rectification measures and submitted them to the Ministry of Finance for review and approval. The measures propose allocating funds to the nitre salt collection bureaus and increasing the price of nitre salt to prevent it from being used for salt production, thereby increasing tax revenue. The Ministry ordered the Salt Affairs Administration to handle the matter. (Special dispatch, 5th)

Liu Lao Jian Lock Project Work Is Hastened

(Nanjing) The piling work at the Liu Lao Jian Lock is progressing slowly due to excessive soil and sand. Efforts are now being stepped up, and it is expected to be completed by early August. The entire project is expected to be completed by the end of October. (Central News Agency dispatch, 5th)

They jointly unsealed the Minghua treasury to inspect the account books. Depositors are determined to oppose the Shanghai headquarters' unified liquidation plan and advocate that the Tianjin branch's external debts be offset by its external debts. The bank's treasury currently has 3,000 yuan in cash. After paying miscellaneous debts, there is a remaining balance of 1,300 yuan. The total Tianjin debt is estimated at over 1.2 million yuan, while the total external debt is 1.35 million yuan. There would be a surplus if liquidated locally. (Special dispatch, 5th)

(Xuzhou) The counties under the jurisdiction of Xuzhou have not received rain for a long time, and the weather is severely dry. Bank Fugitive Apprehended in Suzhou

(Suzhou) Wang Weinong, an accountant at the Silk Industry Bank, absconded with 40,000 yuan to Suzhou. Shanghai detectives learned that Wang was hiding at No. 46 Taohuawu. On the 30th of last month, they went with the Suzhou Public Security Bureau to arrest him. Upon arrival, No. 46 was found to be a nunnery, with only a monk and an incense servant present. The incense servant, named A Gen, stated that Mr. Wang had indeed been there but had gone elsewhere. The detectives instructed him to report immediately when Wang returned. The detectives returned the next day (July 1), but the monk had left, reportedly to Wangting, according to A Gen. Today, the Bureau received a report that Wang was hiding at the home of Pan Chenqing at No. 14 Jiajiafen. They went there this morning and arrested Wang, confiscating over 300 yuan and a watch. A Gen, the incense servant at No. 46, was suddenly assassinated, with three knife wounds in his neck, suggesting a connection to the case. (Special dispatch, 5th)
