China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River Steamer Jiangshun Damages a Pontoon Boat; Anchor Chains Snapped, Damage Significant; Personnel Dispatched for Inspection and Repairs

The Jiangshun, a Yangtze River steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, damaged a pontoon boat when docking in Nanjing on its voyage from Shanghai to Hankou. The damage was severe. Yesterday, the company dispatched personnel to Nanjing for inspection to prepare for repairs. Details are as follows:

Damaged Pontoon Boat

The Jiangshun is the premier large Yangtze River steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, classified as a first-class vessel. The steamer has a registered gross tonnage of 4,327 tons and operates on the Monday/Thursday regular schedule. The captain is an Englishman, W. McIlwaiu. On this voyage from Shanghai to Hankou, it was carrying a large amount of upstream cargo and many passengers. On the 4th of this month, the steamer arrived in Nanjing. As usual, it berthed alongside the wharf to load and unload cargo and embark and disembark passengers. As the captain was directing the docking, a large pontoon boat was moored alongside the Nanjing wharf, held in place by six large anchors, to facilitate the docking of Yangtze River steamers and the unloading of cargo. Unexpectedly, the Jiangshun, through an act of carelessness, collided heavily with the pontoon boat. The six massive anchor chains securing the pontoon boat were snapped by the Jiangshun. The anchors sank to the bottom of the river.

Pontoon Boat Adrift

With the anchor chains severed, the hull of the pontoon boat was also struck. The pontoon immediately broke its moorings and began to drift. The pontoon boat had a very large capacity, originally capable of carrying six to seven hundred tons of cargo. Emergency measures were immediately taken. Dockworkers towed the pontoon boat back to the wharf to prevent it from drifting away. A telegram was immediately sent to Shanghai to report the incident and request prompt repairs to the broken chains to avoid disrupting the regular schedule of steamers. The Jiangshun, due to schedule constraints, continued its voyage to Hankou after loading and unloading cargo and passengers, proceeding upstream as usual.

Personnel Dispatched for Inspection

Yesterday, after receiving a report from the Nanjing branch, the Shanghai head office then received a report from Captain McIlwaiu of the Jiangshun, along with a statement on the matter of responsibility for the collision with the pontoon boat. Upon receiving this information, the head office considered the matter to be of great consequence, and the extent of the damage was still unclear. General Manager Liu Hongsheng instructed the Shipping Department to promptly investigate the matter. The Shipping Department then appointed An Qibang, the head of the retained ship department, to travel to Nanjing yesterday to thoroughly inspect the damage and oversee the repair work. An departed for Nanjing yesterday.

The Truth Behind the Suicide Jump of a Xin Xin Waitress; Stemmed from a Marriage Dispute; Argument with Mother Led to Separation

Tao Guizhen (also known as Ah Feng, age 17), a waitress at the rooftop garden of the Xin Xin Company and a native of Changzhou, suddenly jumped from the roof around 9:00 PM the night before, committing suicide. This was previously reported in this newspaper. Subsequently, after the police from the Lao Zha district took the body to the funeral home on Avenue Petain for examination and dispatched detectives to investigate, it was learned that the woman's mother, Tao Zhang, currently resides at 131 Avenue Foch and earns a living by doing laundry. Previously, the mother and daughter lived together in peace. Unexpectedly, two months ago, the daughter had a dispute with her mother over her right to choose her own marriage partner. This caused a deep rift between the two. As a result, the daughter once attempted to swallow gold in a suicide attempt but was rescued. From then on, the daughter separated from her mother and rented a residence at 43 Mill Street in the French Concession with her close friends Wu Xiuying and Wang Qiaozhen. Around 7:00 PM the night before, she left home to work at the company. Later, a regular customer from Tianjin with the surname Wang came to the company and gave the woman two yuan without ordering tea, then abruptly left. Soon after, the woman suddenly jumped from the building, committing her second suicide attempt. It is unknown why she took this drastic measure. It is difficult to ascertain the reason for this suicide. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, arrived at the funeral home to examine the body. After briefly questioning the woman's mother, Guo concluded that the deceased, Tao Guizhen, female, died of a head injury sustained in a fall. The body was released to her mother, Tao Zhang, who signed a statement to take it back for burial.

Case Against Cheng Linsheng and Others; All Failed to Appear in Court Yesterday; Lawyers Requested a Postponement

Cheng Linsheng and Gan Yize, shareholders of the Gentae Hohe Flour Factory, and Li Quanshen, the manager, were recently sued in the First Special District Court by Xu Yiming, a Cantonese resident of 171 Tangshan Road, Lane 1, House 17, for forgery. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang Zhaoxin of the First Special Court summoned them to the Eighth Criminal Court. All three defendants had lawyers appear in court, stating that Li Quanshen had a sudden case of diarrhea, Gan Yize had been ill for several days, and Cheng Linsheng had gone to Hangzhou on urgent business. All were unable to appear in court to answer the summons and requested a ten-day postponement. Judge Yang reviewed the request and, as the defendants had not appeared, it was difficult to proceed. He granted the defendants' request and announced a postponement.

Juxingcheng Bank Embezzlement Case; Longtime Clerk Implicated; Sued Along with an Employee; Court Opened Hearing Yesterday

Zhang Weiqi, an employee of the Juxingcheng Bank at 276 Jiujiang Road, suddenly abandoned his position and fled at the beginning of last month. After auditing the accounts, Director Yu Yuanhui discovered that Zhang had embezzled 49,126.32 yuan. It was also discovered that Zhang had an account under the name of the Jinti Trading Company at the Jin Cheng Bank, initially depositing 2,500 yuan, and with later transactions exceeding 20,000 yuan. The address listed for the Jinti Company was upstairs at Lin Ji's place on Mill Street. Yu investigated and found that the address was actually the residence of Yu Fujie, the head clerk of the Juxingcheng Bank. Believing that Zhang and Yu were jointly involved in the embezzlement, he sued Zhang and Yu in the First Special Court. After an initial summons, Zhang was ordered to be arrested. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang Zhaoxin continued the hearing, ordering Yu Fujie to appear in court with his defense lawyer, Huang Yuping. According to Yu's testimony, the old clerks and servants of the bank were not allowed to disobey the orders of the bank if the bank had orders, so Zhang Weiqi instructed me to deposit the account at Jin Cheng Bank and write the address of the Jinti Company as my residence. I had no right to question it, and I only followed orders. I had no involvement in the embezzlement. Judge Yang stated that further investigation was needed and adjourned the hearing.

Sister-in-Law Sues Brother-in-Law; Sister-in-Law Could Not Be Summoned for Court Hearing; Judge Instructed the Defendant to Help Find Her

Shen Qianyuan, a Ningbo native from the Sanxing Tobacco Company at 71 Yulin Road, had a seven-year-old daughter after his wife, Rong, passed away. With no one to care for the child, he entrusted her to his sister-in-law, Rong Yuelan, who had married Shi Jianqing and lived at 7 Yulin Road. Shen visited his daughter frequently at his sister-in-law's house. Over time, he and Yuelan became involved. Recently, they had a daughter who is now ten months old. The two suddenly had a disagreement and became estranged. Rong Yuelan sued Shen in the First Special Court for abandoning her and their young child. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang opened the Eighth Criminal Court to hear the case. According to the bailiff's report, Rong's address could not be found, so the summons could not be delivered. Therefore, Rong did not appear today. Shen appeared on time. According to his testimony, although he had a relationship with his sister-in-law, he did not know whether the child was his, because Rong had relationships with other men. He had already paid Rong 100 yuan to end the relationship, but now she was filing a lawsuit. The court believed that if the plaintiff did not appear, the litigation would inevitably be delayed. Therefore, the defendant was ordered to help find her and submit a report to the court after finding her. If her whereabouts could not be found, the court would issue a public notice according to law. The defendant, Shen Qianyuan, agreed to help find her and report back. Judge Yang adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Yan Luqing Imprisoned; Carried Dozens of Books; Prepared for Study in Prison

Zhou Jinggeng, a comprador at the Schmeidel Accounting Firm at 9 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, had his office broken into and robbed of 12,000 yuan in cash on the afternoon of June 9th of last year. The case involved Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Shuyou, Tang Qingyue, and others. The French police arrested them and prosecuted them in the Second Special District Court. The victim, Zhou Jinggeng, appointed lawyer Yan Luqing to appear in court and file a collateral private prosecution, seeking damages. Subsequently, Yan and Zhou extorted 60,000 yuan from the families of Zhang and Zhuang to settle the case but failed. They then extorted 2,000 yuan from the family of Tang. The families reported the matter to the French police, who investigated and confirmed the facts. The police department then filed a public prosecution against Yan Luqing in the Second Special Court for extortion. After a trial by Judge Xiong Huiping, Yan Luqing was sentenced to two years and six months in prison on July 28th of last year, fined 800 yuan, and deprived of public rights for five years. During the appeal period, he was allowed to leave on bail by paying 8,000 yuan. Meanwhile, the Disciplinary Committee of the High Branch Court of Lawyers proposed disciplinary action and decided to suspend Yan from his duties and notify the Shanghai Bar Association to remove him from membership. Yan refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the High Branch Court and the Supreme Court, but both courts rejected the appeal. The Supreme Court sent the case file and verdict to the High Branch Court, which dispatched police to deliver the verdict, as reported in this newspaper earlier. It is now learned that the execution warrant and judgment from the High Branch Court were delivered simultaneously, ordering Yan to report to the court for execution at 9:00 AM yesterday. Yesterday, Yan Luqing reported to the High Branch Court on time, carrying dozens of books, preparing to read and study in prison. Judge Xiong Huiping of the High Court opened the court, summoning Yan Luqing to the front. After briefly questioning his age and background, the judge informed him that the case had been appealed and rejected by the Supreme Court, confirming the original judgment. Today, he was being summoned to the court to execute the prison sentence and pay the fine. Yan responded in the affirmative and stated that his appeal was well-founded and that there was hope for a retrial. However, the court sent the reasons in the judgment, which did not result in a retrial, so he was dissatisfied. The judge then advised Yan that if new evidence were discovered, he could request a retrial. He then ordered the bailiffs to take Yan down and send him to the Second Special District Prison on Rue Massenet for execution.

Case of Obscenity; Yang Jiaju Appealed; Concluded Hearing in Court Scheduled for Sentencing

Yang Jiaju, son of Cantonese lawyer Yang Guoshu, was previously sued in the Criminal Court of the First Special Court by a woman named Shen Yuan for seducing her seventeen-year-old daughter, Shen Shu--, and committing obscenity. She also filed a civil suit seeking damages of 5,000 yuan. The Special Court concluded the hearing and acquitted Yang, dismissing the plaintiff's civil suit. It is now learned that Shen Yuan refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Second High Branch Court. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Yu Huating and Judges Xiao and Shi took the bench to hear the case. The appellant, Yang Jiaju, appeared in court with his representative lawyer, Liang Bohua. The plaintiff, Shen Yuan, did not attend due to illness. The appellant's representative lawyer then rose and stated the grounds for the appeal, divided into two points. The first point was that Yang Jiaju had seduced Shen Shuyun and taken her to the Nanjing Hotel to commit adultery without the appellant's consent. The second point was that Yang had written two notes, causing Shuyun to mistakenly believe that they had a marital relationship, and thus submit to his adultery. The appeal also included the civil suit. Next, Shen Shuyun testified that she was seventeen years old, from Suzhou, born on February 13th of the eighth year of the Republic of China. She currently lives with her mother at 4 Puyutang Street, Taoshachang, in the city. She has nine older siblings, all of whom are married. She is the youngest, the fourth sister. One of her sisters lives in Hong Kong. At the age of fourteen, she went to Hong Kong to study at Ying Wa Girls' School for three years. In August of last year, she dropped out of school and came to Shanghai because of her mother's illness. The defendant, Yang Jiaju, had previously met her when he was friends with her brother-in-law in Hong Kong. On December 5th of last year, she went to her sister's house to play. Yang suddenly called and asked if her sister was home. She replied that she was not. Yang said that her sister was waiting for her at the Dahua Ballroom and that he would pick her up in his car. A short time later, Yang arrived in his car. She unsuspectingly got into the car with him, and they went straight to the Dahua Ballroom. Because she did not see her sister, she wanted to go back. Yang then said that he would go out with her to look for her. She was lured to the Nanjing Hotel, where he committed adultery and broke her chastity. However, Yang stated at the time that he had no wife and was willing to marry her. She was misled by his sweet words and lost her virginity. The next day, they went together to Yang's office on the upper floor of the Shanghai Commercial Trust Company at the intersection of Henan Road and Beijing Road, where Yang wrote a note. Later, because Yang did not fulfill the agreement, she repeatedly went to his office to inquire. She was also repeatedly cheated on. Because the note written by Yang was not effective, she later went to lawyer He Sui to sign another contract, which was certified by lawyer He to prevent future changes. Unexpectedly, Yang still went back on his word, so she filed a lawsuit. She is now asking a lawyer to punish him, not to pursue financial compensation. At this point, the appellant's representative lawyer stood up and said that the case was independently filed by Shen Yuan as the legal guardian. According to her, Yang must compensate her for 5,000 yuan. Yang Jiaju testified that Shen's brother runs a brothel. Because he was forcing Shen to become a prostitute, Shen did not agree and asked me for help. She wanted to be a dancer. On December 5th of last year, I danced with Shen at the Dahua Ballroom and gave her 30 yuan. Afterwards, we spent the night together at the Nanjing Hotel. Later, because her brother intended to extort money, I dared not go out with Shen again. There was no adultery in the office. There are three people in my office, how could I do such a thing? This can be investigated. Under the arguments of the lawyers from both sides, Presiding Judge Yu adjourned the arguments and scheduled the sentencing for the morning of the 12th of this month.

No. 6 Ferry Maiden Voyage; Night Run for Evening Cool Tonight

The Shanghai Municipal Xingye Trust City Ferry Management Office's newly built No. 6 ferry has been under construction since spring and summer by the Hexing Machinery Manufacturing Factory. It was completed at the end of last month. The size and style of the boat are largely similar to the No. 5 ferry, but the sturdiness of the materials and the richness of the decorations are even better than the No. 5 ferry. The maximum speed can reach 13 knots per hour, which is even higher than all other ferries. The boat's interior layout has now been completed. It is scheduled to make its maiden voyage tonight (6th) and operate a night run for evening cool. It will depart from the Beijing Road pier at 8:30 PM. It is expected that ladies and gentlemen will travel together to enjoy the ride.

Case of Fighting and Murder Between Two Chauffeurs; Friendship Turned to Enmity Over a Chess Game; Two Brawls Led to Tragedy

Gu Wenquan, a native of Wuxi, was a chauffeur for a foreigner at the Great Northern Telegraph Company, driving car number 159. Sun Ganquan (also known as Li Afu) was also a chauffeur. The two cars often parked near 34 Avenue Edward VII, so they became good friends with close feelings. On the afternoon of the 28th of last month, Gu and Li, because their masters were in office, gathered to play chess to pass the time. Due to disagreements over the game, they clashed five times. They wrestled with each other three times, but others persuaded them to stop. At 2:40 PM, Sun argued with Gu again, and then they fought. At that time, Gu punched Sun in the face with his fists, causing Sun to lose his balance and fall to the ground. His head hit a piece of redwood on the ground, causing him to be injured and bleeding from his mouth and nose. After the police arrived, Sun was sent to the hospital for treatment, and Gu was detained in the general police station. After investigating, Detective Gao Yanrong of the Shanhua team sent Gu to the First Special Court, requesting detention. However, Sun died at 3:00 PM on the 29th due to his serious injuries. The prosecutor of the First Special Court confirmed that the death was caused by a fall after being beaten. Yesterday morning, the police sent Gu to the First Criminal Court. Police lawyer Ru Bao--- filed the indictment. According to the investigation, Gu did not intend to cause Sun's death, so he was charged under Article 279 of the new criminal code. The family of the deceased then hired lawyer Yan Yinwu to file a civil suit, requesting that Gu be ordered to compensate the deceased's monthly funeral expenses of 45 yuan for a period of ten years. Gu Wenquan testified that the deceased had repeatedly come to beat him, so he punched him in the face. He did not know if he hit him. Presiding Judge Feng Shide reviewed the testimony and, because the two witnesses had not arrived, he ordered a postponement.

Young Woman Insists on Divorce; Unable to Bear Husband's Abuse; Judge's Mediation Fails

Gu Jinlin, a local young woman in her early twenties with considerable beauty, was married to Huang Shouan, who ran a rice shop at 450 Qujiazhai, Gaoqiao Town, Pudong, through an arranged marriage. At the beginning of their marriage, the couple's relationship was fairly good. However, due to trivial family matters, they often quarreled. Recently, the couple's relationship deteriorated further. Therefore, Gu Jinlin could no longer bear it and hired lawyer Pan Zhensheng to file a lawsuit in the local court, requesting a divorce. The lawsuit stated that the defendant, Huang Shouan, was fond of wandering, did not work properly, and indulged in gambling, pawning all of the plaintiff's dowry and clothing. When she tried to persuade him, she was beaten. The defendant's mother, on the other hand, smoked opium all day and night. She often accused the plaintiff of not serving her properly and incited her three daughters to help her beat the plaintiff. She often forced the plaintiff to return to Ningbo to borrow money. If she did not comply, she would first scold the plaintiff for being useless, and then beat her. The defendant's mother and son knew that the plaintiff was covered in injuries, so they locked the bedroom and did not allow her to leave. After the injuries healed, she was restored to freedom. The plaintiff was in this human hell, and the abuse she suffered made it impossible to live together. She attempted suicide by jumping into the river several times, but was rescued. On December 15th of last year, she was forced to return to Ningbo to borrow money. Unexpectedly, after she returned home, the defendant falsely accused the plaintiff of committing adultery and fleeing, and reported her to the court. Fortunately, the court was fair and found her not guilty. The defendant's intention was to insult and harm her. In this situation, the couple's relationship was completely broken. Therefore, she was forced to request a divorce and the return of her dowry. After receiving the lawsuit, the court summoned both parties to a hearing yesterday morning at 8:30 AM by Judge Sun Jikang. Both the plaintiff and the defendant appeared in court with their lawyers. First, the plaintiff, Gu Jinlin, recounted the events and requested that the divorce be granted. Next, the defendant, Huang Shouan, testified that he was twenty-two years old and denied the plaintiff's allegations. He claimed that the plaintiff was lazy and spent all day gossiping and laughing with the neighbors, neglecting her household chores. He had repeatedly advised her that they were a small family and should not waste their time. Unexpectedly, the plaintiff not only did not listen, but also unreasonably made trouble for him. Earlier, she used the excuse of returning to Ningbo to visit relatives and did not return. He went to pick her up several times, but she hid and refused to see him. Recently, she listened to gossip and requested a divorce. However, he was a small businessman and it was not easy to marry a wife. The wedding cost a lot of money, and he asked for a chance for reconciliation. After hearing the testimony, the judge repeatedly tried to persuade both parties, but the plaintiff insisted on a divorce, and reconciliation was hopeless. The debate then began. The judge considered the matter concluded and scheduled the sentencing for 10:00 AM on the 10th.

French Authorities Explain Rickshaw Registration

Regarding the French authorities' implementation of rickshaw registration, there have been external rumors of a restriction on the number of rickshaw pullers. Some individuals went to the French authorities to inquire about the matter. According to them: (1) The French authorities do not limit the number of rickshaw pullers or the registration period. (2) The registration period is divided into several months to avoid crowding. (3) Even after the expiration of this multi-month period, those who have not yet registered can still complete the registration process with the French authorities. The aforementioned three points have already been explained in detail to the rickshaw owners by the French authorities.

First District Party Headquarters Suggests Banning Shop Names Using the Term "Overseas Chinese"; The Meaning of "Qiao" Refers to Being Abroad; Its Use Within the Country is Quite Inappropriate

According to Dagong News Agency, the First District Party Headquarters submitted a document to the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday, stating: "The 27th Sub-branch has reported that various shops in the city often use the term 'Overseas Chinese' in their names, such as Overseas Chinese Sock Factory, Overseas Chinese Bathhouse, Overseas Chinese Store, etc. At first glance, it almost makes one wonder if Shanghai is not part of our country. Furthermore, the meaning of the term 'Qiao' originally refers to residing temporarily abroad. The combined term 'Overseas Chinese' is a common term for our people residing abroad. Conversely, people from England, America, and France residing in our country are also referred to as 'British Overseas Chinese,' 'American Overseas Chinese,' and 'French Overseas Chinese.' It would be appropriate for our people to establish shops abroad using the term 'Overseas Chinese,' but it is quite inappropriate to use it for shops located within our own country. It is not only unsightly but also creates controversy with neighboring countries. Upon examination, other domestic areas do not have such inappropriate and incongruous names. These shops are merely seeking peculiar names without considering the fundamental national identity, and it is necessary to ban them. It is requested that a strict order be issued to replace them within a limited time to improve appearances." The Municipal Party Headquarters, after receiving the report, considered the suggestion to be insightful and decided to send a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau for review.

Lawyers Association Submits Petition to Various Courts Requesting Attention to Safeguarding Lawyers' Duties; Fifty to Sixty People Storm Lawyers' Lounge; Lawyers Cannot Be Subject to Any Interference from the Opposing Party

The Shanghai Lawyers Association submitted a petition to courts at all levels yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of respectfully requesting instructions to pay attention to safeguarding lawyers' duties: According to a letter from member Huang Han, 'Member was appointed by Cen Zhisheng and 65 others in a case against the Tongfu Company Rental Office in the District Court (Civil Case No. 10432 of the 23rd year). Han was commissioned by Ni Jingui of the defendant Tongfu Company Rental Office as a litigation agent. On the afternoon of the 20th of this month at 2 PM, Han appeared in court as an agent. After the court session, while Han was in the lawyers' lounge, suddenly 50 to 60 people from the plaintiff's side stormed into the lounge and questioned Han, saying that he should not attack the plaintiff. Han informed them that lawyers' defense and attacks in court are the lawful exercise of their duties, and if the opposing party has reasons, they can present them to the court. They have no right to illegally interfere. However, the plaintiffs, relying on their numbers and power, raised their hands as if to inflict violence on Han. Fortunately, other colleagues present and the plaintiff's attorney, Yu Hualong, intervened and prevented him from being harmed. The plaintiffs then shouted insults loudly in the corridor outside the lounge, threatening to harm Han. To prevent the situation from escalating, Han had to endure it temporarily. It is believed that lawyers represent litigation according to law, which is a duty entrusted by the state, and they cannot be subject to any interference or intimidation from the opposing party. If this is not stopped by law, lawyers will be threatened everywhere and unable to perform their duties. This matter concerns the interests of the entire legal profession, so we are reporting the facts and asking the association to take preventive measures against the aforementioned situation, and respectfully request a resolution on how to handle it.' The Executive and Supervisory Committee at its 198th joint meeting resolved to submit a petition to courts at all levels for attention and to notify all members. In addition to sending separate letters to all members, we are formally submitting this document to respectfully request your attention, which is in the public interest."

The Crisis of Kala-Azar in Northern Jiangsu

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society on Rennie Road, despite its best efforts to appeal for assistance and provide aid due to the widespread drought last year, has yet to resolve the matter. Unexpectedly, a type of Kala-Azar (i.e. Spleen Enlargement Disease) has broken out in various counties of Northern Jiangsu this spring, which is even more severe than the drought. Once infected, death is certain sooner or later if not treated. The symptoms initially resemble malaria with fever and chills, followed by the formation of lumps in the abdomen. Over time, this progresses to loss of appetite, weakness and emaciation, abdominal pain, night sweats, bloody discharge, blindness, and rotting gums. Those afflicted with this disease are mostly young children and able-bodied adults. Initially, there were only a few cases, which then spread to each other. Recently, the number has grown to over 100,000 people, and the spread is rapid, becoming more widespread and turning villages into ruins. The entire society is facing a precarious situation. Currently, the deadly flames are gradually trending southward, and the future is truly frightening. Although there is a German injection solution that can effectively treat this disease, the medicine is very expensive and requires long-term injections. Treating one person's illness costs no less than dozens of yuan. Bankrupt villagers cannot afford this, and eight or nine out of ten die due to lack of funds for treatment. It has been heard that villagers, unable to afford treatment, are resorting to drawing lots to seek treatment. For example, if a village has Kala-Azar and fifteen people cannot afford treatment, each person will contribute one yuan in cash, accumulating fifteen yuan, and then draw lots. The winner will take this money for treatment, while the remaining fourteen people can only wait for death. What could be more tragic than this in the world? Mr. Wang Shuxiang, a respected member of Northern Jiangsu society, witnessing this tragedy, was deeply moved and painstakingly researched ancient prescriptions from various books. Finally, he fortunately obtained a secret prescription that has repeatedly proven to be remarkably effective, having already cured hundreds of people. Moreover, it is cost-effective and easy to administer, costing less than one yuan to save a life. As a result, patients from various counties, upon hearing this news, flock to seek treatment every day, bringing the elderly and the young. The tragic situation is unbearable to witness. However, Mr. Wang, limited by his personal financial resources, cannot provide treatment to everyone, and feels deeply distressed. Recently, he came to Shanghai in person to request assistance from the Society. However, the Society, having used all its relief funds to assist with last year's drought, can only lament its helplessness. However, if this disease is not quickly eradicated and allowed to spread, it will not only bankrupt the rural economy but also, over time, become a racial problem. It is hoped that kind-hearted people from all walks of life will quickly provide assistance to eliminate this catastrophe. It is reported that Mr. Wang is currently staying in Shanghai. Those interested in researching this prescription or providing financial assistance can inquire at the Society.

Storyteller Assaulted by Ruffians; Sparked by Failed Extortion Attempt

Shan Minggao, a native of Suzhou, has been setting up a storytelling stall near Tangshan Road on Avenue Edward VII, enjoying a thriving business. He attracted the attention of Shen Ronggen (from Ningbo), a local ruffian. The other day, Shen went to Shan and, under the guise of an excuse, extorted ten silver dollars from him. Shan only gave him thirty copper coins, which Shen refused, leading to a verbal altercation. Shen left in anger, saying, "Just wait and see." At around 8 PM that afternoon, Shan was still at the same location, performing his storytelling as usual. Shen Ronggen arrived with a person known as Xiao Mao. Without asking any questions, they dragged Shan out of the crowd and brutally beat him with fists and feet, knocking him to the ground. Xiao Mao then used the wooden signboard he was carrying to strike Shan's head and face repeatedly, causing profuse bleeding. Shan cried out for help. Police Constable No. 1914, upon hearing the alarm, rushed to the scene and arrested Shen. Xiao Mao escaped during the chaos. The injured Shan was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The suspect Shen, along with the signboard, was taken to the Huishan Police Station, where the incident was reported to the station chief and ordered to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Shanghai Municipal Council stated the circumstances and added that his accomplice Xiao Mao was still at large, requesting a postponement. Subsequently, Constable No. 1914 presented the signboard for inspection. The victim, Chen Minggao, testified about the assault. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was evasive, claiming that he only asked the plaintiff for cigarette money and asking for leniency. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered him to be detained and scheduled a new date for investigation.

Lu Shenfa, a Local, Entangled in a Cohabitation Dispute with a Female Tea Server; Falls Victim to a "Honey Trap"

Wu Yueying, a 22-year-old woman from Hangzhou residing at No. 315 Avenue Foch, French Concession, is a female tea server at the New World Company rooftop amusement park on Nanjing Road. She is beautiful and has not been formally married, but she has many male admirers. Lu Shenfa, a local man from Changzhou, residing at No. 3 Linmaoli, Zhizaoju Road, Nanshi, who runs a leather wallet factory, is 29 years old and unmarried. Last month, while visiting the New World Company, he encountered the woman. After being seduced and charmed by her, Lu, considering himself unmarried and the woman seemingly willing to marry him, agreed to become her lover. On the evening of the 22nd of the same month, Lu spent the night at her home and began preparing to cohabit. On the morning of the 4th of this month, suddenly a gangster from Pudong, Wu Hongxiang (30 years old, resident of Caishi), along with several others, rushed to the woman's home. At the time, Lu and the woman were still in bed, not yet having gotten up. Wu immediately claimed to be the woman's husband and accused Lu of adultery with his wife. He first violently beat Lu and then dragged him to a teahouse, demanding 20 silver dollars to settle the matter. Afterwards, Lu believed that the woman and others had intentionally set up a "honey trap" to extort him, and he reported it to the French police. Detective Zhang Xueyong rushed to the woman's home on the morning of the 5th and arrested Wu Hongxiang and Wu Yueying. Yesterday, they were taken to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Lawyer Fei Xizhen of the Police Department requested a postponement of the investigation. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Lu Shenfa, testified, "Last month, I went to the New World Company and met the woman. She said she was not married and was willing to spend her days with me. Because I also have no wife, she asked me to go to her home. I also wanted to marry her. As for the night of the 2nd, I went because it was raining, and she asked me to stay overnight. The next day, she asked me to give her 5 dou of rice, intending to cohabit with her. Later, she wanted me to pay off her debts. Because I learned that she had sworn an oath to a foster father, I stopped going. Her foster father came and demanded 20 yuan from me. Wu Hongxiang also came out, claiming to be her husband, so I didn't dare go again. Later, someone persuaded me to still go and cohabit, guaranteeing that there would be no problems in the future. I felt relieved and went again, and also paid her rent of 14 yuan. On the evening of the 3rd, I stayed at the woman's house. On the morning of the 4th, Wu Hongxiang led many people to catch me in the act of adultery. First, he slapped me twice and then dragged me to the teahouse, demanding 100 yuan to settle the matter. Finally, I paid 20 yuan and was able to escape. Later, I thought that they intentionally set up a honey trap to deceive good people, so I was unwilling to accept it and reported it to the police," he said, completing his testimony with tears in his eyes, filled with endless sadness. Wu Hongxiang confessed that he had been in a relationship with Wu Yueying for three years. The rest of his statement was ambiguous. Wu Yueying testified that the plaintiff did not want her and that her manager, Xiao Nanjing, was asked to mediate and resolve the matter. There was no conspiracy to extort money. After reviewing the testimonies, Judge Li Changnian ordered a postponement of the hearing for ten days and ordered the defendants to be detained.

The lawsuit has dragged on for several years and has not yet been resolved. After several hearings by Judge Cai, the three defendants were ordered to each provide a solvent shop as bail for release pending further instructions. Details were previously reported extensively. It is now reported that Zhao Guanqing was severely beaten while accompanying enforcement officers. Zhao then hired someone to carry him to the court for a medical examination, claiming that he was instigated by Zhang Deming and others to have the workers assault him. Prosecutor Du Jiasheng confirmed that the injuries were real and instructed Zhao to seek medical treatment himself. The other day, Zhang Deming and Cai Qihou, the factory's bookkeeper, were summoned to court for investigation. After the investigation, they were ordered to be detained for further investigation. Yesterday morning, representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau, Tan Peiyan, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yuan Hongjun, as well as Zhao Guanqing, who was still injured, were ordered to attend court, represented by his son Zhao Yangchun. After being interrogated by Prosecutor Du, Zhang Deming and Cai Qihou, who were in custody, were summoned again for further investigation. As a result, Zhang Deming and Cai Qihou were ordered to be returned to custody pending thorough investigation.

Wang Zhongxian's Debut Work "Illustrated Shanghai Slang" Published

Local dialects differ, so their slang also varies. Taking Shanghai as an example, there are no less than a thousand words of slang, which are commonly used in daily life, but their meaning cannot be understood by those who have just arrived in Shanghai. Even those who have lived in Shanghai for a long time can only know what each slang means, but not why. As for the classics, few can answer. The literary scholar Wang Zhongxian has lived in Shanghai for decades and is familiar with the situation of various societies. He has studied slang for many years, so he has written "Illustrated Shanghai Slang". All Shanghai slang is included, and its allusions, origins, meanings, and applications are described in detail. Moreover, one can get a glimpse of the situation in Shanghai and various thresholds. It is a must-read work for people living in Shanghai and those from other places who want to know about Shanghai's local customs. Wang's writing style is light and fluent, lively and concise, and has always been praised by readers, so the description in this book is especially fascinating. The famous painter Xu Xiaoxia is also invited to add illustrations to each article, which is even more icing on the cake. The article was published in the Social Daily and was widely circulated for a while, with countless requests for reprints. Now, in response to readers' requests, it has been finely printed as a separate edition for sale. There are a total of 240 articles, totaling 400,000 words. It is hot-stamped and finely bound, and each volume is sold for 1.6 yuan, and a paperback version is sold for 1.2 yuan. There are not many books printed, so buyers should hurry up. The general distributor is the Social Publishing House in Cian Lane, behind the New-New Company in Shanghai. Mail orders from other places are accepted, and postage stamps are accepted. Add one cent for postage.

Bansong Garden in Nanshi recently launched the Night Flower Garden because of the hot weather and the lack of a high-end summer resort for Shanghai residents. The preparations have been made so far and have cost a lot of money. The beauty of the garden has long been famous. Recently, various new and valuable entertainments have been added, such as the Brilliant Boat, Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, Chinese and Western Fireworks, Moving Lanterns, High-end Literary Tiger, etc., which are unique and ingenious. Starting today, the opening hours will be extended day and night until 12:00 midnight. Tickets are still sold for 20 cents. Long-term travel tickets are only sold for one yuan. A special travel magazine is published every day, with a detailed map printed to facilitate tourists to find their way according to the map at a glance. Chinese and Western dishes and various cold drinks are specially prepared in the country, and the prices are low. The Nanshi tram extends the time to facilitate transportation. It is expected that the opening today will be a grand occasion with heavy traffic.

Inspection Report of China Agricultural and Industrial Bank

The June inspection report of the Shanghai District Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank stated that the issuance exchange coupons and reserve funds of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank in June of the 24th year were inspected on July 5th, the 24th year of the Republic of China, by the directors and supervisors, together with the accountant Tang Zaizhang, the leader of the coupon line, and Zhang Xietang, the representative of the village. The inspection results are listed as follows: The total amount of exchange coupons issued was 5,415,657 yuan. The total amount of exchange coupon reserve fund was 5,415,657 yuan, including 3,847,515 yuan in cash reserve and 1,568,142 yuan in guarantee reserve. The above two reserve items, the cash reserve accounts for 71% of the total, and the guarantee reserve accounts for 29% of the total. All inspections were accurate and consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby made.

Minxian Zheng Zhong's Metal and Stone Carvings

Zheng Zhong, a famous metal and stone artist, whose style name is Rujun and whose sobriquet is Ya , is skilled in seal script and official script, and is especially good at carving books, imitating Qin and Han, unrestrained without losing the rules. His chapter method and knife method are all profound. His best work is the "Jijiu Zhang". Mr. Zheng recently collaborated with General Li Du to carve two seals, which were published in the Great America Evening News by Mr. Zhu, a friend of Mr. Zheng. The seals used by famous calligraphers and painters in China, such as Yu Youren, Zeng Yunpei, Chen Yichan, Yang Weiquan, and Liu Aisheng, are mostly made by Mr. Zheng. All the experts give good comments , so it can be known that Mr. Zheng's seal making is very skilled. Mr. Zheng lives at No. 29 Tiancheng Lane, Xuehuali Road in Shanghai. Gentlemen of broad knowledge can visit him.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory forecast the weather at 4:30 PM yesterday, saying that Shandong is clear and sunny all around, with winds coming from the southeast to southwest. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy, with showers and northeast winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy, sometimes cloudy, with intermittent drizzle. The southeast wind is quite strong. There are cyclones and fog or rain south of Ma'an Island and in the East China Sea due to the passage of low pressure eastward. Taiwan is cloudy all around, with fog and uncertain winds. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 81.1, and the lowest was 70.7. On the same day last year, the highest was 87.7, and the lowest was 76.3.

Letter

Dear Sir, I read a news item in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on July 1, which stated that "Artificially dyed green jadeite was found in the Shanghai Jade Market". After investigation, it was found that it was not in accordance with the facts. The dyed emerald horse-eye was accidentally purchased by me. After it was identified, it was submitted to the market affairs council for inspection and confirmed to be true. According to industry regulations, the owner of the goods, Gu Yisheng, was fined as an example. Your newspaper mistakenly published that I was the owner of the goods, which is not in accordance with the facts. However, merchants value credibility the most, so I dare not remain silent, and I specially write this letter to ask you to correct it and clarify the truth. This is for the consideration of the editor. Respectfully, Wang Jinchang, July 5.

Special Article Liu Haisu Reports on His European Tour (7)

2. This Promotion of Art Education Enhances China's International Status: Those with short-sighted views only hope that a good diplomat can use some magical means to enhance China's international status. This is just a dream! China is now a very poor nation, which Europeans know well. Europeans believe that China's situation is: the Communist Party is causing trouble, the economy is bankrupt, bandits are kidnapping people, the politics are dark, the culture is backward, and there are natural disasters such as floods and droughts! In addition to using economic aggression plans, they have looked down on China for a long time. Our so-called diplomats have no "status" internationally, so we can't blame them for not daring to speak. This is not a problem of people, but of a bad environment. To enhance China's international status, it is important to solve various problems, but it is even more urgent to promote the Chinese Renaissance movement. Because the development of modern European nations has always gone through great art and thought movements. The countries that are now called strong in the world are also the nations with developed modern cultures, such as France, Britain, Russia, Germany, and Italy. Before their national power was developed, there were always many great thinkers and artists who engaged in great thought and art movements with an indomitable spirit to inspire the public's independent and strong personality and independent and fearless development. Because great artists and thinkers are the soul of a nation. This can be proved by the fact that the exhibition of paintings in various countries has aroused the respect of people from various countries for the Chinese nation. The summary of the criticism published by the German "Future" newspaper on February 11, 1934, clearly represents the opinions of the most numerous audience: "...For the first time, without a catalog or explanation, I wandered through this beautiful forest of paintings for three hours without preparation, and I only felt dazed in a dream. There is such a higher and more excellent world in the universe, which is higher and purer than ours. It is like the ideal country of our great poets and artists 120 years ago. This intelligent nation is now being brutally bombed by some strong and armed countries. But it is still alive and existing very happily. I hope to go to China, accompany these people with supreme harmony and intelligence, learn everything from them, and tell people about their exquisite paintings... The second time I accompanied a country woman who, like me, had not studied or painted, but she also had sensibility and subtle feelings, and she had the same beautiful impression as I did. The third time I met a soldier who also collected all the new and old paintings, and he also hated and excluded outsiders like me, but here he also smiled, bowed his head, and accepted others sincerely. How can he bomb and destroy this cultural country? He repented and realized that such a transcendent and noble nation is inviolable..." Also, Dr. Kong William, a German art historian, said sincerely in his commentary published in the Berlin Daily: "...China is now not peaceful, and the great Central Plains has suffered setbacks. The philosophy that has been盛傳for thousands of years has been shattered, and Western science and industry are singing a triumphant song. But the soul of China is immortal, because painting is one of the greatest creations of the Chinese spirit. He has always preserved the characteristics he created and is evolving forward, and his deep roots provide nourishment to keep him alive forever. This is also a symbol of the Chinese nation..." Also, when the Chinese Modern Painting Exhibition was held in England, the British also had hundreds of criticisms. The editorial published by the Times on March 30, 1935, attracted international attention. Here is also an excerpt from it: (to be continued)

The Children's Year Implementation Committee Resolved to Request the Change of Primary School Spring Vacation to Start from April 5 to Facilitate the Celebration of Children's Day

(Nanjing, 5th) The National Children's Year Implementation Committee held three general meetings at the Ministry of Education on the 5th. Chen Heqin and 20 others attended. Gu Shusen, the chairman, reported on the handling of the resolutions of the previous general meeting and resolved: 1. Approve the method of holding the opening ceremony of Children's Year, and ask the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Department, the Central Propaganda Committee, the Health Department, and the Organization Preparatory Committee to proceed as soon as possible. 2. Contact Liu Shirong of the Central Propaganda Committee to make a feature film of the Children's Year song. 3. Ask the Children's Education Group to revise the methods for newspapers and magazines to publish Children's Year special editions or weekly magazines. 4. Ask the Children's Education Group to revise the methods for the National Children's Toys and Teaching Aids Exhibition and the Children's Reading Materials Exhibition. 5. The committee will compile methods to ask various bookstores to compile and print Children's Year commemorative books and distribute them to children at low prices. 6. Recommend Chen Heqin, Pan Gongzhan, and Hu Shuyi to draft an outline of various activities for children during Children's Year. 7. Ask each group to draft a compilation and transfer of publicity booklets, and the deadline for collecting manuscripts, and submit them to the committee for review. 8. Ask the Ministry of Education to change the date of the primary school summer vacation to start from April 5 to facilitate the celebration of Children's Day, and ask to revise the school holiday regulations. 9. Ask for a children's sports plan. 10. Set July 31 as the date for another general meeting so that all members can participate in the opening ceremony of the National Children's Year. 11. Ask the Children's Welfare Group to revise the organizational outline of the Parents' Association. 12. Approve the organizational outline of the Children's Problem Consultation Office in principle, and the committee will submit it to the Ministry of Internal Affairs and Education and the Department of Health to jointly conduct a trial run in the central government, and then promote it to other places. 13. Recommend Zhu Zhanggeng, Chen Heqin, Hu Shuyi, Luo Yunyan, and Gao Junshan to draft organizational methods for national children's welfare institutions and a phased implementation work plan, and the committee will submit them to the Ministry of Internal Affairs and Education for review by the Executive Yuan for implementation. 14. Set the meeting for 9:00 AM on the 6th for group meetings and 10:30 AM for the general meeting.

Municipal Education Bureau Scheduled to Hold the Ninth Primary School Teacher Registration Starting July 10 for Three Days Applications with Incomplete Procedures Will Not Be Accepted

The Municipal Education Bureau, in order to be cautious about the qualifications of teachers, will hold the ninth primary school teacher registration for teachers who will be hired to teach in various primary schools in the 24th academic year. It is hereby determined that registration will be held for three days from July 10th to 12th. When registering, applicants should fill in two registration forms, submit their graduation certificates and service certificates, and bring three recent two-and-a-half-inch photos. Graduates of this year's normal school who have not yet obtained a graduation certificate after participating in the entrance examination must submit a school certificate. Applications with incomplete procedures will not be accepted. Physical examinations will be held at the Nanshi Public Stadium on the 13th, and oral examinations will be held at the Municipal Wanzhu Primary School in Jiumudi on the 14th. It is reported that those who have passed the eighth general registration do not need to register this year. Also, those who have passed the non-trial and assessment of the fourth primary school teacher and have undergone physical examination can be exempted from re-examination.

Municipal Education Bureau Orders the Shutdown of the Shanghai East Commercial Vocational School

The private Shanghai East Commercial Vocational School on Beiwener Road in Shanghai was founded by Zhang Zhenmin and others. It was taken over by Chen Si on the 7th of last year. It is reported that it has not gone through the filing procedures according to law, all facilities do not meet the regulations, the qualifications of the teachers do not meet the requirements, and there are only eleven students. The content is extremely corrupt. The board of directors has been reorganized seven or eight times in a year, and the principal has also been changed seven or eight times. It has also illegally sold amusement tickets, treating education like a child's play, which is harmful to society. After investigation by the Municipal Education Bureau, it has been ordered to end and shut down before the end of this semester.

Principal He Bingsong of Jida University Issues Statement: Detailed Account of Accepting the Appointment and Future Management Policies for Jida University

—Shanghai Alumni Association Recommendation for Mr. He—

The position of president of National Jinan University has been filled by the central government's appointment of Mr. He Bingsong. Yesterday, our reporter made a special visit to Mr. He, who kindly issued the following statement:

Since returning to China after studying in the United States in the fifth year of the Republic [1916], I was introduced by Mr. Cai Yuanpei to Peking University and Beijing Higher Normal School, where I served as a lecturer in history for many years. It was not until the eleventh year of the Republic [1922] that, at the urging of Mr. Jiang Menglin and others, I went south to establish Zhejiang First Normal School and participate in the planning of Zhejiang University. At the time, I found it quite difficult to cope. Later, I was introduced by Mr. Wang Yunwu and Mr. Zhu Jingnong to the Commercial Press, where I worked as an editor and translator for more than ten years, which suited my personal interests. Therefore, in recent years, I have repeatedly declined invitations from Mr. Yang Duanda, Mr. Zhou Gengsheng, and Mr. Zhu Liuxian. This spring, I was honored to serve as the chairman of the China Academic Society, planning the affairs of the society, and I felt even more that my knowledge was insufficient.

Recently, Minister of Education Mr. Wang Xueting and various members of the board of directors believed that the position of president of Jinan University was of great importance and insisted that I take on the responsibility. I consistently declined due to my limited talent and learning, but they did not agree. At the same time, the Shanghai municipal party and government authorities also repeatedly urged me, making it impossible for me to refuse. Now that the official appointment has been announced, it concerns serving the country, and a national university is of great importance to national culture. Therefore, I cannot stubbornly decline and must comply. I will temporarily resign from the Commercial Press to devote myself to the duties of president.

As for the improvement of university affairs, I previously consulted the central government and have since given it detailed consideration. I deeply feel that there are many threads to unravel. For example, regarding curriculum issues, in addition to the need for fundamental reorganization and no longer creating courses based on individual instructors, how should we focus on cultivating teachers for Nanyang [Southeast Asia] and researching Nanyang commerce, in order to realize the special mission of Jinan University? Also, regarding financial issues, in addition to naturally ensuring absolute transparency, how should we plan for a reasonable allocation to ensure the balanced development of research work in all departments and colleges of the university? Furthermore, regarding the equipment of books and instruments, in addition to urgently enriching the essential parts, how should we strictly comply with regulations to effectively supplement them so that all teachers and students have abundant research materials? Moreover, regarding the overseas cultural affairs, which are greatly related to our country's future outward development, how should we plan various research methods, objects, and purposes to conduct them effectively, in order to contribute to the country? Furthermore, regarding the attached secondary school, where most students are children of overseas Chinese, how should we focus on modern national training to live up to the trust of their parents? All of these matters cannot be decided without gathering experts and deliberating at length. I am currently starting the research and will prepare a report within a set time, selecting the key points to be submitted to the ministry for approval and implementation.

As for whether an atmosphere of academic research can be created throughout the university and whether the academic performance of all students can be greatly improved, it all depends on whether the professors are suitable for their positions. Therefore, the issue of selecting professors for the entire university is of utmost importance. I have carefully considered this and prepared a list to be submitted to the ministry for approval. Once the instructions are received, formal invitations can be issued, and so on.

Jida University Students Qiu Zhizhong, et al.: Suggestions Made

Guowen News Agency reports: The Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University, based on its goal of promoting the development of its alma mater, specially dispatched representatives Qiu Zhizhong, Xu Fu, Xie Huaiqing, Chen Ranmo, Cai Cixue, Li Jingbo, Li Jialin, et al., to meet with the newly appointed President He Bingsong at 10:00 AM yesterday to suggest ten opinions on reforming university affairs. Mr. He came out to meet them and, in principle, fully accepted the various suggestions made. The following is a record of Mr. He's responses: (1) He fully accepted the request to thoroughly reorganize the curriculum to ensure that it aligns with overseas Chinese education and enhances the academic atmosphere. (2) He fully accepted that the hiring of teachers should be based on profound scholarship and abundant writings, and that full-time teachers in the major departments should account for two-thirds of the total. (3) Regarding the funds for purchasing books and instruments, he agreed to set it at 15% of the total university expenditure, exceeding the request for one-tenth. (4) He fully accepted the implementation of a budget and final account system for finances and the monthly publication of accounts. (5) Mr. He stated that from now on, he would fully ensure the security of employment for faculty and staff and implement a seniority-based salary increase system. (6) He fully accepted improving administrative efficiency to promote mutual progress within departments. (7) He accepted in principle the rapid establishment of work-study and free student quotas to cultivate impoverished students, and that more scholarships may be established in the future. (8) The selection of outstanding graduates each year for further study abroad would depend on future financial conditions. (9) Regarding effectively guaranteeing the positions of students serving at the university and employing and introducing newly graduated students as much as possible, Mr. He stated that students currently serving at the university would be retained entirely if their performance was not particularly poor, and that newly graduated students would be employed and introduced as much as possible. The representatives presented Mr. He with a list of over ninety students currently serving at the university. (10) Regarding the request to allow overseas Chinese students graduating from the attached secondary school who have passed the entrance examination to enter the university department without further examination, he said he would consider it and then implement it, and so on.

Children of This City: Return Gifts to American Children: 10,000 Items Collected by the Education Bureau; Reply Letters Printed and Ready to be Sent to the United States

The American World Children's Friendship Association, in order to promote friendship among children worldwide, sent a large number of American drawings last year. The local Education Bureau distributed them to elementary school children in this city and collected return gifts, totaling 10,000 items, which are scheduled to be sent out by the end of this month. The details are as follows:

Return Gifts: All 10,000 return gifts to American children have been collected by the local Education Bureau. They include the Children's Morning News Special Edition on the Construction of Greater Shanghai, which features copperplate-printed photos of construction in this city, as well as photos of Chinese scenery and handicrafts made by elementary school children, such as shuttlecocks, and portraits of Sun Yat-sen. Each item has 10,000 copies. Reply letters to American children, printed in both Chinese and English, have also been printed. The cover features the Chinese and American flags, and the back cover features a photo of Director Pan of the Education Bureau, the leader of the children of this city. The printing is exquisite, and the packaging of the various gifts is also quite elaborate.

Reply Letter to the United States: Dear American children, we received your large letter last year and many beautiful pictures, which allowed us to see the famous mountains and rivers of your country, inspiring our imagination. We are extremely grateful and delighted. Our Shanghai is mistakenly praised by various countries as the fourth largest commercial port in the world. Our dear American children must be thinking about it. Now, we will tell you about its general situation. Shanghai covers an area of 1,600 square li and has a population of over 3 million. It is located at the midpoint of our country's coastline, bordering the Yellow Sea to the east and connected to the Yangtze River, the Shanghai-Nanjing, and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways to the north. There are steamships going back and forth with major commercial ports around the world, making water and land transportation very convenient. In terms of scenery, there are Fanwang Pagoda Garden and Bansong Garden, which are very lush with trees. In terms of commercial areas, there are Nanshi, Zhabei, and the concessions. Since the success of our National Revolution, the government, considering that the commercial area is too far from the harbor (Wusong), making it inconvenient for merchant ships to enter and exit, began constructing the central district of Shanghai in the 20th year of the Republic [1931], realizing our ideal plan for Greater Shanghai. Now, the municipal government and its bureaus of health, public works, social affairs, education, and land have moved into the new buildings in the central district in the 23rd year of the Republic [1934] to conduct business. Residents' houses and roads have also been built one after another. There are also sports fields, libraries, schools, etc., which are also being actively constructed. In Wusongkou, wharves are being built to facilitate the loading and unloading of goods by merchant ships from various countries arriving at the port. The Nanjing Road area is the most prosperous for commercial business, followed by Zhabei, and then Nanshi. Shanghai has a population of over 3 million, and children account for three-tenths of the total. Among them, some have not yet entered school, because our country's elementary school system in the past did not implement a compulsory system like other countries around the world. However, it will gradually be improved in the future, so that every child in the country will attend school. As for the elementary school curriculum, in addition to the national language, arithmetic, history, geography, nature, hygiene, and civics, there are many extracurricular reading materials. Among them, the most popular is the Children's Morning News. This newspaper is half pictures and half literature, and its content is very rich. It strives to include any material that is beneficial to children. Reading it not only brings us endless fun, but also greatly benefits our studies. Therefore, almost every elementary school student in Shanghai already has a copy. The two newspapers we are sending you this time are the Children's Morning News. We have said too much. Are you annoyed? However, we have an ancestor, named Laozi, who had two famous sayings: "The rich give wealth, the benevolent give words." Therefore, we sincerely hope that you will not mind the distance and often communicate with us to guide us and report good news to us. We would be very grateful. Finally, we have prepared some gifts for you, which are listed on a separate list, so we won't say more here. As for the making and using of shuttlecocks, we have specially asked the Children's Morning News to publish a special issue to send to you, which you can understand at a glance. "A goose feather sent from afar is a small gift but full of affection." Please accept our sincerity. Goodbye, and wish you happiness. The children of Shanghai, Republic of China, bow.

Municipal Wuben Girls' High School: New School Site Determined; Admissions on the 7th and 8th of This Month

Municipal Wuben Girls' High School is the oldest girls' school in this city, having been established for 34 years. Recently, due to the old school buildings and small grounds, renovation was inconvenient, and expansion was impossible. Therefore, Principal Yan Zhenyu consulted the Education Bureau to plan a relocation and construction project. It is now known that it has been approved by the Municipal Government and the Municipal Education Bureau. A site of over fifty mu has been selected next to Zha Yin Road in the central district, with a construction cost of 350,000 yuan. Construction is scheduled to begin next semester, in preparation for moving into the new buildings during the winter vacation. In order to ensure that the construction and equipment of the new school buildings fully meet the ideals of modern girls' education, Principal Yan, along with the heads of various departments, visited famous high schools throughout the city this semester to learn from their experiences. It is also known that teachers, students, and alumni of the school will organize a committee to raise funds for a memorial hall to commemorate Wu Huaijiu, the founder of the school, at the site of the new buildings, to serve as a place for alumni gatherings and for teachers and students to improve their moral character and relax. It is expected that in half a year, the only municipal girls' high school in this city, beautiful and magnificent, will stand in the new urban area and become a model for girls' schools throughout the city.

In addition, it is reported that the first admissions of new students have been scheduled for registration on the 4th, 5th, and 6th of this month, with the examination starting on the 7th. As for transfer students for all grades, they will not be admitted because the quota is already full.

Zhaohe Middle School: Zhaohe Middle School in this city was founded in the 21st year of the Republic [1932]. Most of the founders are important figures in the central party and government. Yang Hu, director of the Security Bureau of this city, is particularly responsible in practice. The school was originally established to commemorate the Fourth Year of the Republic [1915] campaign against Yuan Shikai, in which Yang led the Zhaohe warship to launch an uprising, a glorious revolutionary history. The main purpose is to cultivate useful youth and provide them with practical and rigorous training to instill the knowledge of the new era. Therefore, the tuition fee is particularly lower than ordinary schools, equivalent to that of provincial middle schools. In the past two years, the number of students has increased significantly, and school affairs have progressed rapidly. Last semester, Mr. Yang resolutely accepted the election of the board of directors and became the headmaster. He has spared no effort in promoting school affairs in the past six months. As the original school address on Lubangsheng Road was located in a factory area, which affected the physical and mental development of students, a new school building and dormitory for boys and girls were specially leased and built at 990 Xujiahui Road. The construction is also underway. The teachers and staff hired next semester are mostly full-time and are graduates of famous universities at home and abroad. The new school site was originally the villa of a senior foreign military officer. The building is magnificent, and the location is secluded. It has now been fully moved into the new school site on July 3rd and is scheduled to recruit new students for the first time on July 15th.

Lehua Middle School: Lehua Middle School in western Shanghai, originally named Lehua Girls' Middle School, built its own school buildings in Fahuazhen at the end of Xiafei Road last year. It admits both boys and girls, and there has been a surge in applicants. It is reported that after being registered by the Municipal Education Bureau, there have been many applicants. It is planned to purchase more than 30 mu of vacant land behind the school at the beginning of the next semester to expand the school buildings.

Graduates of Jiangxi Vocational School Sent to Jiangxi Province

This year's graduates of the business department of the Jiangxi Advanced Vocational School in Nanshi, this city, over twenty in number, have been sent to the International Trade Bureau, Guohua Bank, and other places for internships. Another part has been introduced by Principal Xu to the Jiangxi Department of Finance for employment, as the province is currently reforming the accounting system of various counties and needs new-style bookkeeping talents and accounting statistics talents. It is estimated that those who have been introduced include Huang Qikang, Hu Yunhai, Hu Xianquan, Xia Jinshui, Yan Yongwei, Xie Fengchun, Wei Yonggui, Li Chuansong, Xu Risheng, Zhang Yigui, Zhou Zuoqing, Wang Ziyi, Luo Dashen, Li Fengqi, Xu Renzhi, and others, totaling fifteen people. Finance - The Bullish Front Wavering - The Gold Market Filled with Selling Pressure - Resulting in Another Fall of Ten Yuan and One Fen -

The gold market suddenly experienced a period of fluctuations yesterday, mainly because the bullish sentiment wavered, and many floating orders were executed. Confidence waned, and prices nearly fell to the 820 yuan mark. However, due to continuous heavy buying by large players and a reduction in Indian silver imports, the market finally stabilized somewhat. Early in the morning, news came from overseas that the US market was completely closed. Only large gold bars in London remained flat for both near and far terms. Forward silver in Montreux rose by 2.5 to 3 percent. Exchange rates rose slightly. Spot gold in London fell by 7 pence. When pre-market trading opened, it immediately fell to 32.3 yuan, failing to maintain its position. Large players took the opportunity to sell bars, soon breaking the 30 yuan mark and retreating to 28 or 29 yuan. The Central Bank's announced prices were flat for both British and American currencies. The customs gold unit fell by 7 cents. The listed standard price for gold was 863.2 yuan. Afterwards, supply and demand from large players were inconsistent, and there was much struggle. The morning opened with low prices, and the market continued to weaken after the opening. However, buyers maintained support at low prices, resulting in some rebound. The exchange rate announced by HSBC was flat for both British and American currencies, and the market hovered without direction. In any case, banks' appetite remained full, and the foreign exchange market hardened. Sellers continuously moved, gradually pushing prices lower. The Hong Kong market also loosened accordingly. Confidence was strangely timid, and bullish positions continued to be unloaded. There were also some short-selling flows, resulting in extremely strong selling pressure and a rapid decline. Later, banks took advantage of the cheap prices to buy back in, and large players vigorously purchased at low prices, resulting in some rebound. However, confidence had not yet stabilized, and the trend at noon remained weak. The market immediately trended downward after the afternoon opening. However, in general, large players continued to buy heavily, leading to a prolonged struggle. Unexpectedly, the Indian silver report showed a small reduction of one anna, causing sellers to feel disappointed and being pulled up. Although there was some oscillation, the banks' appetite was strong, and buyers repeatedly moved, while short-sellers took the opportunity to enter, resulting in a rebound. The source of supply was still abundant even after the rise, leading to a slight pullback. However, confidence had stabilized. Call Money Shows Slight Easing

Interest rates remain unchanged: Copper coins increase by another 1,000.

Yesterday's silver dollar market situation: The government's relief loans have been actually distributed. However, only a few have benefited slightly due to collateral issues. Ultimately, this sudden increase in a large amount of funds in the market has somewhat supplemented the current financial situation. Therefore, the situation has gradually eased, and the long-unchanging call money rate has gradually declined, showing slight easing. The opening immediately fell by one dime, changing to five dimes, and finally closed at four dimes and five cents, a decrease of one dime and five cents compared to the previous market.
