Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Xu Xiaoting)

The slight drizzle does not necessarily seep into the house, and the complex and diverse society does not necessarily corrupt young people. To prevent rain from entering the house, it is necessary to repair the leaks. To prevent young people from falling, it is necessary to instill appropriate knowledge.

Opposing chastity is the characteristic of romantic women, and opposing reading is the characteristic of degenerate youths. In fact, women who seek a life within the confines of chastity may sometimes be unchaste. Young people who seek knowledge in a reading environment may sometimes not seek knowledge. It depends on human effort. Circumstances make heroes, and the environment can sometimes change one's nature.

Although economic subsidies are necessary to help the countryside, attention must be paid to seed improvement and fertilizer research. Thinking from one aspect is dead, while thinking from multiple aspects is alive.

Women and Beauty

— Zhang Huang

As long as a woman is in her youth, she is beautiful for several years, but most of them are unaware of it.

Among women, if someone is truly very beautiful, or very lively, or truly very dashing, they will definitely be aware of it!

Women can discover beauty in the same sex better and faster than men. They can admire the beauty of the same sex with sincerity, without a trace of jealousy, unless there is a special reason.

Naturally, they most want to have beauty themselves and do their best to achieve "having all the beauty, without any lack of beauty." The so-called "daughters love themselves naturally" does not necessarily have any purpose, such as the "women dress for the pleasure of men" mentality. Therefore, they are often afraid that youth will fade away. Each woman probably does not hesitate to increase the consumption of cosmetics with age, even if she is still in her youth, in her radiant period. If someone teases her and says, "I haven't seen you for a few days, and you seem to have lost weight! Relax a little, it's not worth making yourself look so tired!" She will definitely believe this person's words and become suspicious of herself. Also, if someone compliments an old woman in her thirties or forties and says, "Why are you always so young! If you pay a little more attention to dressing up, wouldn't you still be in your wonderful teenage years?" I know that although she usually laments and hates the gradual aging of her appearance, she will thank this person for correcting her long-held hypersensitive misconception, making her suddenly wake up. You know how much inexplicable joy is added to her heart at this time, and at the same time, she praises this person as the only one who understands, even if she is humbly on the surface: "Oh, we are old women!" Ah!

In fact, the relationship between women and beauty is much greater than that of men. But look, the voices of women transmitted on the phone or on the radio are mostly delicate; the figures of women walking on the street are mostly charming. If you don't meet them face-to-face, you won't want to turn around and take a look. This special gift is the lifeline of women!

I sympathize with the special beauty of women here and wish that all the girls in the world will become angels, amen!

Be Careful

— Juan Yin

Characteristics

— (Hua Ling)

A foreigner, traveling in Asia, ended his journey in Canada. He has some wonderful discoveries for every place.

Indeed, his wonderful discoveries are sometimes unspoken by others and are often overlooked by other travelers.

This is naturally very interesting, so I am now excerpting a few of them below:

Penang - Everyone speaks English, but if you ask any "Englishman", the result is always a Scotsman.

Colombo - Full of nothing but cunning merchants.

Australia - There are hot meat buns and hot coffee. Java - That is a city that no one loves, but the suburbs have a population overload.

British Malaya - The streets are clean, flat, and obviously strictly managed, and the air is obviously solemn.

Siam - That is a place where fighting fish are used to determine victory or defeat.

Burma - The color of religion is thicker than any country in the East.

China - People do not have a fixed time for eating and the number of meals. They can chat for the whole day.

Shanghai - That is a gorgeous city, the nightlife is never ending.

Japan - Everyone is polite, hardworking, and skilled in technology.

Canada - The vibration of the train is particularly severe, often making people feel frantically hungry in their stomachs.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: Bitterly Persuading with Sincere Words, Not Just Empty拍案, The Sound of Money and Shadows of Lamps Pitifully Sells People

Zhiqian thought to himself that there were probably countless similar things happening in the Tu Hai Hotel, so why bother worrying about this one? So he pulled a book out of the net basket and put it under the lamp to read. He had only read two lines when he said to himself that it wouldn't work and loudly called for the tea attendant. The tea attendant brought in a kettle of boiling water and asked if he wanted boiling water. Zhiqian said: I don't want boiling water, I want to ask you something. In Mr. Zhang's room, many people were gathered just now, and there was the sound of foreign money, what were they doing? The tea attendant smiled and did not answer. Zhiqian said: It seems that Miss Zhu has already been sold to that man named Jia, right? The tea attendant laughed and said: It's not really selling! It's just giving a gift of fifty dollars and taking the person over. If it were a sale, Mr. Jia could pay more money. Because the Zhu family just didn't want to sever ties, Mr. Jia said that there would definitely be a lot of burden in the future, so he didn't add money. However, he still had to spend a sum, so it was agreed that tonight, the money would be handed over and the person would be handed over at the same time. Mr. Jia has plenty of money, he just treats this little bit of money as if he had spent it on prostitution and doesn't care about it. Zhiqian said: The person will be sent over tonight, why so fast? The tea attendant said: They have already handed over the money, if the person is not sent over, how can he agree? He paid the money so happily, isn't it all for the sake of... The tea attendant saw that Zhiqian's expression was not good and left on his own. Zhiqian, on the other hand, clearly felt that this matter had nothing to do with him, but he felt very uncomfortable in his heart, as if he were drunk. He couldn't read the book, and he couldn't sleep, so he just sat under the lamp feeling depressed. After about an hour, he heard someone knocking on the back door of Little Western Paradise from afar. Following that, the tea attendant in the courtyard walked to the back door. (258)

Records of Floating Imperial Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The prescriptions that the four imperial physicians prescribed to the Empress Dowager generally had twelve kinds of medicinal herbs, about half of which were the same, and half of which were different; in total, there were more than twenty kinds. The Empress Dowager looked at their prescriptions one by one, and as she looked, she asked the old eunuch about the properties of the various herbs—there were also a few that she herself had always known, so there was no need to ask again; there were also a few that she knew, but was not sure of, or had forgotten, so she had to ask the old eunuch. In this way, she selected what suited her best and wrote it down. When she had picked out twelve, she would no longer pick any more. So the writing eunuch used another piece of white paper and respectfully wrote down the twelve herbs that her old self had picked out. In this way, the fifth prescription was created. This fifth prescription combined the strengths (?) of the original four prescriptions and was a collection of them. One, two, or three or four herbs from the original four prescriptions were used in it, so it could also be said to be a mixed prescription; but the Empress Dowager did not pay attention to whether the properties of these herbs, which were not originally on the same prescription, were compatible or conflicting, nor did she let the four imperial physicians take them away to study them. However, if this mixed prescription caused any problems, the four imperial physicians could not escape responsibility. No wonder I was almost so surprised that I cried out when I watched from the side.

"Now that the prescription has been written," the Empress Dowager looked at me and said, "Deling, you should go this time! When those four stupid medical officers are preparing the medicine for me, you must carefully supervise them!" (358)

Newspaper Seller A Wu

— Bai Ding

Every day, when the sun just climbed up the east mountain, not long after, A Wu, who lived by selling newspapers, would get up hurriedly from the bed made of only three planks, put on a tattered shirt with seven holes and eight patches, and without even washing his face, he would hurriedly cross his tired feet and set off towards the general assembly point for newspaper sellers - Wangping Street. Every day, he rigidly practiced this, no matter how bad the weather, whether it rained, snowed, or was a big wind, there was no need to say, he would go out in the wind and rain as usual. He understood that this was for living, for eating, if he didn't do this, he would have no food to eat, and no life.

Years of hard work had worn A Wu into a consumptive ghost: his two eyeballs were deeply sunken in their sockets, his face was as pale as if there was no blood in it, his cheekbones were high, his dry lips, and his gaunt chin suddenly made him look like a monkey.

So, his companions gave him the nickname: "Monkey A Wu."

The bell had only rung six times, and ninety-nine percent of the people were still sweetly sleeping in dreamland. However, A Wu had already distributed the newspapers he had just picked up from Wangping Street to each household like a revolving lantern.

A Wu is a hardworking person. In addition to delivering newspapers for people in the morning, he had nothing to do in the evening, so he had to sell some evening newspapers, shouting and selling like flying in the streets and alleys, of course, that was also regardless of wind and rain.

According to what he told me, even with such frugality and diligence, his family could not get enough to eat, because in addition to himself, he also had a father in his sixties, a wife, and two children?

Pitifully, a few days ago, he had a fever all over his body from being hit by the wind and rain. He really couldn't support himself to deliver newspapers, so, these days, the one delivering newspapers was his fifteen-year-old child who was both small and weak!

Small Gardening

Miscellaneous Notes on Yumberry

— Red Sheep

Yumberry is also a kind of fine fruit in midsummer, with a purple color and plum flavor. It is shaped like a small spiny chestnut, without skin and with a pit. It is on the market after the Dragon Boat Festival. The best yumberry is as big as a walnut, with a color like a purple ribbon, juicy and coreless, with a sweet and clean taste, without the drawbacks of sourness and astringency. Among the fruits, it can be called a delicious one.

There are many places that produce yumberry. The ones produced in Dongting Mountain in Taihu Lake, Suzhou, are as famous as Zisha loquats. There are also many products in Lanxi, Zhejiang, and other places, and the quality is no less than that of Dongting. There is also a kind of white yumberry, which is slightly smaller and flatter than the purple one, with a pit as small as a soybean. The sweetness is like honey, which is even better than the purple one, but the production is not large. Except for the local people, who can taste it, it is rarely seen elsewhere and cannot have this kind of deliciousness.

The usual way to eat yumberry is to first wash the yumberry with cold boiled water or sand-filtered water, and then add a little salt flower to melt on the top of the yumberry. This can kill the insects that parasitize on the yumberry. This is also because the yumberry has no skin, and insects are easy to parasitize on the vegetables. Salt has the effect of disinfecting and killing insects, so there is this way of eating. In addition to the yumberry sold on the market now, there is also a kind that is chilled with ice. When eating, it feels even more fragrant and refreshing. But this way of eating ice-chilled yumberry did not start today. It already existed in the past. Wu Kuan's yumberry poem has the line "If you want to know how cold and good it is, a thousand pieces are recommended on an ice plate", which is ironclad proof of ice-chilled yumberry.

There are many good stories about yumberry. During the Three Kingdoms period, "When Yang Xiu was nine years old, Kong Rong pointed to the yumberry set up by his father and showed Xiu said, 'This is the fruit of your family,' and Xiu responded and said; 'I have not heard that the peacock is a bird of the master.'" During the Liang Dynasty, "Ren Fang was the prefect of Xin'an, and the county had the honey ridge that produced yumberry. It was formerly collected by the prefect, and Fang stopped it immediately because the collection was very dangerous and there were many poisonous things." During the Qi Dynasty, "The yumberry in Wang Xuzhi's courtyard had three fruits in the middle of winter, which people said was caused by filial piety." These are all good stories of the time.

There are also many other names for yumberry, such as Lizhu. "Lu You's poem, 'I don't love the full ship, only the fire, I was surprised to find Lizhu.'" Heting, "Xu Jie's poem, 'I broke off the red Heting, and dug out the dragon's eyes before the blood was dry.'" Saint Monk, "Qian Que Lei Shu records that Yangzhou people call white yumberry Saint Monk." Red fruit, "Guo Zhengxiang's yumberry poem, 'Red fruit decorated with green branches, shining on the front house.'" Jindan, "Bing Ke's poem, 'Looking at the big tree in the cloud pond, trying Jindan in the Xia room.'" Maru Tan, "Xu Jie's poem, 'The green pill is small under the leaves in March, and the Maru Tan is round on the branches in May.'" Sui Zhu, "Li Dongyang's poem, 'The name is from the transmission, and the price is more expensive than Sui Zhu.'" These are all famous other names for yumberry.

According to "Xi Hu Ting Shi", Yangmei Wu in Hangzhou is located in Rui Feng Shi Wu near Nanshan. There is an old woman surnamed Jin, whose family's yumberry is very prosperous, commonly known as Yangmei Wu, the so-called Jin Po Yumberry. It can be seen that Hangzhou also produces yumberry, and it is named after people. Naturally, it is a good kind of yumberry, but now, there is no longer any name of Jin Po Yumberry, and even the place name of Yangmei Wu in Hangzhou does not exist. This is really the vicissitudes of the yumberry producing area.

"Gui Er Ji" states that the Min scholar went to the imperial examination, and the Wu scholar went to the adjustment, each boasting about their native products. The Min said lychee, and the Wu said yumberry. There is a topic on the wall that says, "The jade girl in Min Township contains ice and snow, and the star king in Wu County drives a big cloud." From this record, the yumberry in Wu County can be compared with lychee, and it has long been famous throughout the country, and it is not from today.

Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Radio Waves Under the Direction of Quantum Theory

— Hao

Before the invention of quantum theory, the most powerful theory to explain electromagnetic waves was the wave theory. Since Einstein invented the theory of relativity, quantum theory has established a solid foundation based on it and overturned part of the wave theory. So, how does quantum theory explain electromagnetic waves?

It says: "We know that all matter in the world is composed of atoms, and an atom consists of a nucleus and several electrons surrounding it. Electrons orbit the nucleus at a speed of 2,200 kilometers per second. Since the speed is so high, its centrifugal force must also be very large. But why doesn't it fly out? It is because of the attraction between the free protons and free electrons in the nucleus. The magnitude of the attraction is related to the distance. Therefore, when an electron moves from an outer orbit to an inner orbit, or from an inner orbit to an outer orbit, it must release or absorb considerable energy. Since electrons are the smallest unit of all matter in the world, then the ability to absorb or release energy is naturally the smallest unit of energy, called a quantum. These emitted quanta are emitted in all directions at a speed of 300,000 kilometers per second. The number of groups of quanta emitted per second is the frequency of this electromagnetic radiation. The distance between two adjacent groups of quanta is the wavelength of this electromagnetic radiation. If the frequency is between 60,000 and 1,500 kilocycles, it is a shortwave radio wave; at 1,500 to 600 kilocycles, it is a broadcast radio wave."

The above is just a brief explanation. If you want to study it in detail, please refer to books specializing in quantum theory. Due to space limitations, it can only be omitted here.

Piezoelectric Headphone

— Pao

When a substance with piezoelectric effect is subjected to pressure or tension, a voltage is generated on its surface; conversely, if a voltage is applied, its physical state changes. Utilizing this feature, if a voltage that has been modulated with music is applied to a piece of material with piezoelectric effect, a corresponding change in physical state will occur. If this change in physical state can be used to agitate air by means of a mechanical structure, the original music sound can be obtained. A piezoelectric headphone is made based on this principle, and its structure is completely different from that of an ordinary magnet headphone.

The piezoelectric headphone is produced by The Brush Development Co. in the United States, and its appearance is as shown in Figure A. The material with piezoelectric effect used in it is Rochelle Salt Crystal (sodium potassium tartrate), measuring five-eighths of an inch square and 0.01 inches thick. The entire headphone weighs only six ounces.

The sensitivity of this type of headphone is extraordinarily high, with a impedance of 50,000 ohms at 1,000 cycles; its working frequency range can be from 60 cycles to 10,000 cycles. When connected to a radio, the connection method is different from that of ordinary headphones, as shown in detail in Figure B. The choke coil or resistor in the diagram is used as the plate load for the final vacuum tube.

German Television

— Yan

While American television has not yet been realized, television broadcasting has already begun in England and Germany with the help of the government. Other European countries are imitating them, and it can be said that Europeans are experiencing an intense television craze.

In Berlin, two ten-inch diameter copper rings have appeared in the sky at a height of four hundred and fifty feet. Since then, television has become a popular term rather than a specialized one. These two copper rings are the antennas of the "Berlin Television Broadcasting Station." The ultra-short waves with fifteen kilowatts of power are broadcast from this unique antenna, which can reach an area of about fifty miles around. Each television broadcasting station has two broadcasting machines, one is an ordinary sound transmitter, and the other is a video transmitter. Radio receivers or television viewers also use a special receiver to receive the signals. The screens of these receivers are of two sizes: four inches high and six inches wide, or ten inches high and twelve inches wide.

The adjustment of television channels is very easy because there is a seven-meter space between the wavelengths of the two television stations. This means that there are very few stations in this band. The selectivity of the receiver is not a problem, and there is no interference even if two television stations broadcast at the same time.

The "Berlin Television Broadcasting Station" has been broadcasting on a wavelength of seven meters for nine months. The images displayed are black and white, but they usually have a slight blue or green tint. If television stations all use the "180-line manner" like the "Berlin Broadcasting Station," then not only the head but also the movements of the whole body can be displayed.

The price of each video transmitter is from 250 to 500 US dollars. Television receivers can be divided into two parts, one for receiving sound and the other for receiving and displaying images. The cathode ray tube is the main component of the video receiver.

Recently, Germany built a television van. There is a standard motion picture camera on the roof of the van, which can rotate freely in all directions. The hollow camera support is used to transport the filmed footage to the darkroom inside the van body. Using special equipment and rapid chemical reactions, the film is developed. The undried film is divided into 180 lines by the abtastgerat, and each line has a different intensity of current. The image transmitter broadcasts this picture into the air, and radio viewers can receive it.

Characteristics of the Latest Dual-Function Vacuum Tube 1C6

— KMK

Since the advent of dual-function vacuum tubes, amateur enthusiasts have been eager to experiment and research with each other. This type of vacuum tube not only provides us with great convenience in its operation but also takes up little space, making it extremely convenient.

The 1A6 vacuum tube is one type of dual-function vacuum tube, and it contains a total of five grids inside. Its detailed characteristics have been introduced in this publication many times. Its standard use is specifically for DC superheterodyne radios. It can be used for first-stage detection and local oscillation, etc. However, in order to save power, the current of each electrode is designed to be low. When used in a superheterodyne radio, as long as the accessories are properly matched, there will naturally be no problems in operation. However, using this vacuum tube in an ordinary regenerative radio cannot achieve satisfactory results. Therefore, in order to improve and refine, manufacturers in various countries have successively introduced the 1C6 vacuum tube. The structure of each electrode inside is the same as that of the 1A6 tube, the only difference being that the current of each electrode is slightly stronger.

The filament voltage of the 1C6 vacuum tube is 2 volts, and the filament current is 120 milliamperes (twice as strong as the 1A6). The maximum plate voltage is 180 volts, the plate current is 1.5 milliamperes, the screen grid voltage is 67.5 volts, and the current is 2 milliamperes. The first grid is the input electrode of the oscillation circuit, the second grid is the positive grid of the oscillation circuit and is used to replace the plate of the oscillation circuit, the current is 0.11 milliamperes, the third and fifth grids are the suppressor grids, and the fourth grid is the high-frequency current input electrode. As for the arrangement of the electrode pins, it is the same as the 1A6. This vacuum tube is not only used in superheterodyne radios with amazing results, but can also achieve considerable results when used in other applications.

Amateur Notes

— Liu Tongkang

It goes without saying that everyone knows that a volume control in a radio is used to adjust "overload."

Although ordinary adjustment of regenerative capacitors or filament variable resistors can also increase or decrease the volume, this cannot be considered a good method, and it also reduces the sensitivity of the radio, weakens the effectiveness of the vacuum tube, and damages the filament.

Installing a volume control in the low-frequency amplification stage to limit the input voltage is relatively stable and safe, but difficult problems arise one after another. When this method is used in a radio with multiple stages of high-frequency amplification, the detection stage will be overloaded and produce distortion.

Adjusting the screen grid voltage of the high-frequency amplification tube to control the volume seems to be more effective, but it is not a perfect method either.

At present, the most widely used and effective volume control method is to adjust the C-bias voltage of a variable-mu high-frequency amplification tube to control its amplification factor, while simultaneously increasing or decreasing the antenna input power.

However, in DC radios, after all, due to the structural relationship of the vacuum tube, there are not many applications of this method. In fact, this is not difficult at all. The example introduced here is shown in Figure 1.

V is the high-frequency amplification tube, C is a 0.001 MFD fixed capacitor, R is a 5,000 ohm fixed resistor, RFC is an 85 MH long-wave high-impedance coil, C, is the C-bias (its voltage must be determined according to the vacuum tube, such as No. 43, then 22.5 volts must be used), Ri is the volume control, and the resistance is about 50,000 ohms-100,000 ohms.

Steps for Assembling a Radio for the First Time (2) (Continued)

— Xuelun

(3) Power Transformer

A power transformer is also called an AC-DC converter. Its function is to step down AC mains voltage to A voltage to supply the filaments of the vacuum tubes, and another step-up or step-down coil rectifies its current to B voltage to supply the plates of each vacuum tube. Therefore, the power transformer is the power hub of a radio, and the design must be prepared, and the structure must be solid, so that the radio can work legally and last for a long time. The construction content is not only poor in materials, but also the voltage and current are not suitable for our self-assembled radios, so it must not be purchased.

The detailed design method of the power transformer is recorded in this journal and various magazines, so I will not repeat it here. The power required for this machine is about 60 VA, which can be wound by yourself according to the table below. If beginners feel that it is not easy to make by themselves, it is better to entrust a domestic manufacturer to make it.

Asia-America or Zhongyong No. 2 steel sheets to 40 mm thick, weighing about two pounds.

A set of No. 22 iron clips

Primary 220 volts, use American standard No. 26 enameled wire to wind 938 turns.

Secondary high voltage 600 volts, use American standard No. 32 enameled wire to wind 2456 turns, draw the center tap.

Filament 6.3 volts, use American standard No. 18 enameled wire to wind 26 turns, draw the center tap.

Rectifier filament 5 volts, use American standard No. 16 enameled wire to wind 21 turns, draw the center tap.

When winding by yourself, first take a hard cardboard to make a spool, the inner area is 32 mm × 40 mm, soak in molten wax, wrap one or two layers of insulating cloth, then wind the primary winding, and then wrap one or two layers of insulating cloth on the outside, and then wrap a layer of cigarette tin foil on the insulating cloth, the two ends must not be in contact, one end is connected to a wire, and the iron core is grounded. This kind of installation can avoid a lot of AC noise. The secondary high-voltage coil is wound outside the primary winding, and is still insulated with insulating cloth. The outermost layer is wound with two low-voltage coils, insulated with wax paper. After all the coils are wound, insert the steel sheets one by one, and tighten the iron clips. The power transformer is made. (To be continued)

Publishing World

National Movement and Cultural Movement

— Ye Qing

People engaged in the national movement often despise cultural movement, thinking that it is a way to pull people into the library. Not only is it unrelated to opposing imperialism, but it also shifts public attention and disperses public strength. Therefore, they not only despise cultural movement, but even curse it.

On the other hand, people engaged in the cultural movement do not understand the significance of the national movement and often think that it is just a way to shout slogans. They advocate saving the country through education and saving the country through science. In the era of the "September 18th Incident," they cited Hegel in the Battle of Jena and called on people to learn from him and concentrate on reading and writing books.

These are all biased and obscured. In fact, the national movement and cultural movement should be unified. Why? Because practice cannot be separated from theory, and theory cannot be separated from practice. They must be

combined with each other to form a complete life course.

Then, the national movement depends on the cultural movement.

First, the so-called national movement should be the movement of the majority of oppressed nations. This requires a theory to awaken everyone, unify their will, and align their steps. However, oppressed nations are often backward nations, and the intellectual level of most of their people is very low. Therefore, spreading theory must be formed into a movement. And there is also the need to improve the intellectual level. This, of course, must be achieved through cultural movement.

Second, the imperialism invasion of oppressed nations has a theory as an excuse, such as the superiority of races, the civilization of backward nations, which sounds very good. And it also uses Christianity to numb the masses and run schools to create foreign slaves. At this time, oppressed nations must have a theory to confront it. If it does not expose its mask, even its own unity will feel difficult because its consciousness is conquered by imperialism.

At this point, isn't it obvious that oppressed nations should have their own cultural movement? This is the starting point and tool of their national movement. The era of the Boxers has passed, and the way of primitive riots and simple xenophobia are no longer needed.

On the other hand, cultural movement also depends on the national movement.

Culture is a tool for human beings to adapt to the environment in order to make a living. When oppressed nations are invaded by imperialism, their survival becomes a problem, and they should link cultural movement with the national movement. That is to say, cultural movement should become a type of anti-imperialist movement.

In this way, the line of cultural movement must be the national movement. In other words, it is the declaration of the spiritual independence and freedom of oppressed nations. Therefore, it should take opposing imperialist culture as its slogan. The Western culture or European culture that people generally talk about is imperialist culture. Hu Shi's welcoming of Western culture and Chen Xujing's complete Westernization are just flowery words and sweet talk that call us to become spiritual slaves of imperialism automatically. Cultural movement with the national movement as its line must oppose the foreign slave comprador in its anti-imperialist consciousness in the culture of oppressed nations.

After the interactive integration of the national movement and cultural movement, both sides will benefit. In terms of the national movement, with conscious masses and guiding theory, it will be modernized and easy to achieve success. In terms of cultural movement, it will have an independent consciousness and a creative spirit, and can keep pace with advanced countries in the fields of discovery and invention.

Here, if the foreign slave comprador who willingly promotes the culture of European imperialism in China sneers at my discovery and invention, I will answer: You have become a lackey of imperialist culture! According to it, white people are the darlings of heaven, and colored people are born inferior. Now you do regard yourself as inferior, and you don't even dare to have the ambition to discover and invent. You are too worthy of being a slave of a fallen country. What about us? We want to be human, we want to fulfill our responsibility for culture, we want to create culture.

Can backward nations create culture? Yes. I have proved in the previous issue of this publication that backward nations can create culture as long as they start from the cutting edge of world cultural development. What about European philosophy, science, and literature? Critically absorb them, eliminating their dross and absorbing their essence. For philosophy, we want new materialism and abandon everything else; for science, we want natural science, and take more facts and less theory for social science; for literature, we want the best of technology and consciousness. As for the new buds that contain the future culture, we will use them as a creative model, promote and glorify them. In short, let oppressed nations get rid of the pain of spiritual colonies and gain the free development they deserve in culture, and from then on become one of the promoters in the advancement of world culture. Isn't this the responsibility of us—people in oppressed nations—who are engaged in cultural movement?

Anyone who does not dare to say that they can create culture, please withdraw from the cultural world. Let us raise the banner of anti-imperialist culture and declare the spiritual independence and freedom of the Chinese nation!

Several Indexes of the Peiping Library

— Shilue

(1) Index of National Studies Papers

(2) Index of Literature Papers

(3) Index of Chinese Geography Papers

At present, the compilation methods of Chinese indexes are diverse, and no precise and detailed format has been produced yet. Therefore, when we cite a certain index, we must first understand the editing and indexing methods and its characteristics of this index before it can be useful. The indexes compiled by the Peiping Library, according to the above, have a commonality. Generally, their materials are taken from magazines; their nature is considered a specialized discipline; and their arrangement is based on the content of the articles for classification. Therefore, we can call this type of index "Specialized Classified Index of Magazine Article Titles."

The only feature of this index is to provide researchers in this discipline with great convenience in referring to magazine articles. For example, if we want to study a certain problem in this discipline but don't know where to start, then we can check a certain category in the index; then, from each entry in the category, "follow the clues," and through analogy, the problem can be easily solved. Because of this research method, in terms of depth, one can know the true historical evolution process of the problem; in terms of breadth, one can explore the main points and opinions of various schools—thanks to the editor's preliminary efforts, the articles with the same content are grouped together, the researcher is not only spared the effort of random searching, but also avoids the hard work of blind searching!

However, "classification" has no standard rules in today's Chinese bibliography, especially in papers. I am afraid that even after thousands of years, it will be difficult to establish an immutable rule. Therefore, general bibliographers call "classification" "artistic" rather than "scientific." Therefore, it is almost impossible for a classified index to be perfect and flawless in everyone's eyes; moreover, many papers contain multiple problems, and many are difficult to summarize into a certain category—in this way, it is difficult for the compiler, and it is not easy for the checker. Therefore, when we want to cite this index, the first thing we have to do is to know clearly the categories it divides. Below, I will briefly describe the three books separately.

The Index of National Studies Papers has been published in three series. The first series was published in July 1929. The editor is Mr. Wang Chongmin. Mr. Wang is versed in national studies and is proficient in bibliography. The postscript claims that the editing of this book began in the summer of 1925. It collects 82 magazines, with 3,000 plus papers. Since July 1928, the writings of national studies in the past two or thirty years have been generally collected and compiled. Its classification is: 1. General; 2. Classics; 3. Linguistics; 4. Archeology; 5. History; 6. Geography; 7. Schools of Thought; 8. Literature; 9. Science; 10. Political Science and Law; 11. Economics (attached to Currency, Industry, and Commerce, etc.); 11. Sociology; 13. Education; 14. Religion; 15. Music; 16. Art; 17. Bibliography—this category combines Chinese and Western, transforms the old rules of the Four Treasuries, and marks it with names that adapt to the times. After that, the sequel and the second series followed this pattern, and each subcategory was slightly changed. The sequel was edited by Mr. Xu Xuchang. Published in July 1931. Collect more than 80 chapters. The number of papers is roughly the same as the previous series. The third series was edited by Ms. Liu Xiuye. Published in October 1934. Collects 192 magazines and newspapers, and the number of papers is about twice as many as before. A "Table of the Founding Years of the Collected Publications" is added at the end of the volume, which seems superfluous.

The Index of Literature Papers has been published in a sequel. The first series was published in January 1932. According to Mr. Wang Chongmin's preface, this book and the Index of National Studies Papers were compiled at the same time. It was initially compiled by Mr. Zhang Xinyu, and then by Ms. Chen Biru and Ms. Li Zhixuan of the Peiping Library Index Group. A total of 162 magazines and chapters are collected. From the 31st year of Guangxu to December 1929. The book is divided into three series: upper, middle, and lower. The upper series is a general discussion of literature. The general outline of its classification is: 1. General Theory; 2. Meaning and Origin of Literature; 3. Nature of Literature; 4. Classification of Literature; 5. Literary Trends of Thought; 6. Literary Creation; 7. Literary Criticism; 8. Literati; 9. Literary Research Methods; 10. Literature and Others; 11. Literature of Various Countries. The middle series is a specific discussion of literature. Its outline is: 1. Poetry and Ballads; 2. Rhapsody; 3. Ci; 4. Opera; 5. Fiction; 6. Myths and Stories; 7. Children's Literature; 8. Others. The lower series is a critical biography of writers. Its outline is: 1. Critical Biographies of Chinese Writers; 2. Critical Biographies of Japanese Writers; 3. Critical Biographies of Indian Writers; 4. Critical Biographies of Russian Writers; 5. Critical Biographies of British Writers; 6. Critical Biographies of French Writers; 7. Critical Biographies of German Writers; 8. Critical Biographies of Italian Writers; 9. Critical Biographies of American Writers; 10. Critical Biographies of Spanish Writers; 11. Critical Biographies of Polish Writers; 12. Critical Biographies of Dutch Writers; 13. Critical Biographies of Norwegian Writers; 14. Critical Biographies of Danish Writers; 15. Critical Biographies of Writers from Other Countries and Collective Biographies. There are five appendices: 1. Literary Teaching Methods; 2. Literary Items; 3. Introduction to Literary Books; 4. Introduction to Literary Figures; 5. News from the Literary World. The sequel was edited by Ms. Liu Xiuye. A total of 193 magazines and chapters are collected. Published in November 1933. The content of the collected materials continues the time of the previous series to May 1933, and the division of volumes and classification are roughly the same as before; the subcategories have also been slightly changed. However, this book additionally includes ten literary works, namely: Collection of Chinese Literary Debates, edited by Li Helin; Modern Chinese Women Writers, compiled by He Yubo; Outline of Chinese Literary History, compiled by He Kai; Collection of Literary Essays, written by Guo Moruo; Collection of Literary Freedom Debates, edited by Su Wen; World Writers Biographies, compiled by Sun Songgong; Modern Chinese Writers, compiled by Qian Xingcun; Modern Chinese Women Writers, compiled by Huang Ying; Modern Chinese Women Writers, compiled by Caoye; Modern Critical Biographies, compiled by Modern Bookstore—according to this matter, it is to break the precedent. The ten books collected include collections of papers, miscellaneous biographies, and literary histories, which are different in nature; and each book is not an outstanding masterpiece. Moreover, if Li compiled the Collection of Chinese Literary Debates, and the papers in Guo's Collection of Literary Essays are mostly those that have been included in the previous series—in this way, it is not only contrary to the previous style, and the selection of books is not refined, but also has the suspicion of repetition before and after; I think the editor has not thought about these things?

Index of Chinese Geography Papers. Published in April 1934. The book has two volumes. Co-edited by Mr. Wang Yong and Mr. Mao Naiwen. The magazines collected are from the 28th year of Guangxu to July 1927. The nature of the content papers is not purely limited to geography. All those who describe the natural state and humanistic facts of the region have been included. Its main categories are: 1. Topography and Travel Notes;—Geotext (attached to Antiquities)! 3. Ethnic Groups; 4. Politics; 5. Transportation; 6. Economy; 7. History; 8. Geographical Books. (attached to Chinese Geography and Geographers). At the end of the volume, there are two indexes of place names and authors. It seems that this compilation will enhance its convenience in citation compared with the previous two books.

In addition, I heard that the library also has two major works, the Classified Index of Articles in Qing Dynasty Literary Collections and the Index of Stone Inscriptions, which are still in the process of printing and compilation. It is expected that they will be released to the public soon. (May 24)

Records of Impressions of Various Bookstores (Continued)

— Li Hengzhi

Twenty-Two: The Author's Bookstore

In Peiping, there was an "Author's Bookstore," and in Shanghai, there is the Author's Publishing House. The natures of the two are somewhat different. In the Peiping-Tientsin area, there were several "teacher-writers" (because not all were university professors, they couldn't be called professor-writers) who either had no place to print their books, or were being exploited by bookstores, or thought that their books used as textbooks would definitely sell well. So, they organized an Author's Bookstore, investing their own money to print books and handing them over to their own bookstore for sale. The Author's Publishing House also arose from the need for "authors to publish their own books." The difference between it and the Author's Bookstore is that the Publishing House itself is entirely of an intermediate distribution nature, unlike the Author's Bookstore, which is an author's organization, somewhat similar to a publishing cooperative.

In foreign countries, publishers and distributors already have quite specialized organizations, but in China, the Author's Publishing House is still an innovation. It is said that the owner of the Author's Publishing House was previously the director of the Commercial Press consignment department. The Commercial Press took advantage of its many branches and great reputation to ensure the sales of consigned books, and because there were many booksellers who relied entirely on Commercial Press books for their business, they naturally dared not neglect their accounts with the Commercial Press. Therefore, consigning books to the Commercial Press would not have the worry of "not being able to recover the accounts." Now, in addition to the World Book Company, there is the World Publishing Cooperative and the Dahua Book Company for this reason. Since the January 28th Incident, the Commercial Press's consignment department was abolished, perhaps because the person in charge saw the development of the Commercial Press consignment department's business and thus formed the Author's Publishing House themselves. If so, there is indeed a need for consideration in terms of business.

First, the Author's Publishing House cannot be compared to the Commercial Press consignment department. What the Commercial Press consignment department relied on was its numerous branches, and the booksellers in the interior who depended on Commercial Press books for their livelihood dared not delay their accounts, so there was no problem at all with regard to (1) how to promote the books to various places, and (2) how to recover the accounts. But what does the Author's Publishing House rely on now?

Second, if the Author's Publishing House consigns books to various distributors in the interior, difficulties will inevitably arise in terms of discounts and payments. The authors themselves think that handing over their books to the Author's Publishing House for distribution at half price is already as cheap as can be, but if they are then handed over to interior distributors, receiving payment at half price is considered the highest price. Moreover, even if the interior distributors sell the books, they may not immediately hand over the payment, but most authors will not understand this point. This is a serious contradiction, and the first to bear the brunt is the Author's Publishing House.

Third, since the general cultural level in China has not reached a higher level, the number of books published by private individuals and "non-publishing" organizations is not large. It seems very difficult for the Author's Publishing House to rely solely on this as its main source of business. If it still relies on distributing publications from "people in the book business" as its main business commodity, then it is no different from ordinary consignment bookstores—in fact, the Author's Publishing House is gradually tending to go down this road.

Fourth, recently, the consignment business of various bookstores has become increasingly developed. Because their publications are widely advertised, they easily attract readers. For example, the Life Bookstore, the Kaiming Bookstore, and others seem to have surpassed the Author's Publishing House in terms of consignment scope. This may well be a major blow to the Author's Publishing House.

Under these circumstances, it is difficult for the Author's Publishing House to succeed. The Author's Publishing House has been established for two or three years, and its failure to fully develop is probably limited by these objective reasons.

Is the Author's Publishing House itself not a publisher? There is no impression to speak of, but its business method is novel and sufficient to attract people's attention. It is often heard that someone suggests that Shanghai bookstores establish a joint sales method, and this method can be considered in light of the situation of the Author's Publishing House.

Li Hengzhi's Notice—Most bookstores generally consider the end of June as the end of the accounting year. I plan to investigate the business situation of various bookstores over the past year as a reference for the publishing industry in the future. I earnestly request that various bookstores provide detailed information on the following points over the past year: (1) the number and types of books published, (2) the amount of business, (3) all difficulties, and (4) future plans. After some slight整理, it will be published in this journal. This matter concerns the future of the publishing industry, and I hope that various bookstores will do their best to help it succeed.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Truly Unwilling and Unavoidable

— Chen

The newspaper reported the other day that the Lao Beimen police station recently dispatched patrol police to search for prostitutes soliciting customers along the Minguo Road and Xinqiao Street area. Due to some reason, only two were caught. They were taken to the station for questioning, and so on. The number of prostitutes in Shanghai not only dominates East Asia but can also be said to be the champion of the world. According to statistics from Professor F. of Yenching University, there is one prostitute for every 130 people. Whether this is accurate or not is unknown. But last September, the Public Concession authorities only took three to five days to arrest over two hundred and thirty or forty people, causing the new and old women's prisons in the Municipal Council to be packed to the brim and reeking. This is probably something readers still remember. From this, we can easily imagine that if all the prostitutes in the Minguo Road and Xinqiao Street area were brought to the police station's detention center, it could immediately be "packed to the brim and reeking."

Although this spectacle has not manifested, it tells us the tragic state of this urban pathology. From the confessions of these two prostitutes, we know that they have parents above them and children below them. In order to "support the whole family," they "unavoidably" and "truly unwillingly" resorted to this last resort. I think, without talking about human inequality, just starting from humanitarianism, one cannot help but say that the life of a prostitute is twelve thousand times more miserable and painful. The daily life of seeing off the old and welcoming the new is already equivalent to physiological, mental, and self-trampling, not to mention the layers of dark exploitation and exaction in between. Really, except for those "Pan Jinlian seeds" who are inherently lewd in the world, no one wants to enter this fiery pit, but for the sake of life, it is "unavoidable."

This is the same as the state of suicide. Although everyone knows that life has supreme value, when "everything is empty" or "when people are poor, their ambitions are short," they "unavoidably" go to self-deliverance; Jia Yin is also the same. Everyone knows that making the body a commodity is the most tragic thing, but if you don't take this "last resort," you can only starve to death.

Returning

— Juefu

It was a summer evening. The blood-red, proud sun, although still lingeringly hanging on the distant peaks, but the summer's unique evening breeze had already taken away all the heat.

A-Qie, who had eaten many years of grain, with a happy heart, dragging an injured leg, not knowing how many mountains he had climbed, how many rivers he had crossed, the one mountain 　　　 in his mind day and night, was finally glimpsed by him at this moment.

In that one mountain 　　　, hidden a small village of five or six families, in the village was A-Fu's home. Left in his home, was a wife, a son, a mother over sixty years old. He had buried more than thirty years of his life there, every tree there, every stone, every winding and indistinguishable path, he remembered them all: even seven or eight years ago, when he was dragged away to eat grain, how many chickens, how many goats were left in his home... he could still recite these very clearly now. -This home, no, this whole mountain 　　　, he loved it extremely!

He walked many days, and although his body was now exhausted, he was still very happy, very excited, he couldn't wait to jump into that large forest next to the hillside. While 　　　 walking, he was secretly planning: Mother is probably cooking? That one is probably still cutting firewood in the mountains? Little Fuzi might have grown as tall as himself? Dad is afraid that he won't recognize his son? ... A wanderer who had been missing for so many years, this was a sudden return, when Mother saw him, she would surely be overjoyed, no, she would shed tears; when that one saw him, she would surely cry, maybe even scold; even the whole village, would probably cause a small commotion because of his sudden return. He had to tell them what he had experienced

Page 20

everything, he had to state his future plans, wishes, ... all to them, until he taught them to "turn their tears into laughter!" ...

As he thought about this, the smiling expression that had said goodbye to him long ago, now unknowingly floated back onto his gaunt face. He was extremely happy, his whole body and mind, were completely melted in the long river of happiness!

He opened his twice-lost eyes, looking around in the east, looking around in the west, as if he was looking for something he loved most. He compared everything he saw in front of him with the one shadow left in his mind; he always hoped to find something from this comparison to prove the accuracy of his memory. But he failed in the end, the scenery in front of him, looked somewhat unfamiliar to him. He remembered that going forward from the foot of the mountain, there was a foot-wide mountain road, lying on the left side of the mountain road, was a five or six mu large rice field; he also remembered that no matter what evening, looking from the foot of the mountain, he could often see wisps of smoke, floating from the top of the dense green forest, he could see flocks of goats, surrounding their owner, running around everywhere on the hillside, and sometimes he could hear dogs barking, cows mooing, children's noisy voices, ..., but now? The mountain road could not be found, the rice field had disappeared in the weeds: the smoke was gone, the goats could not be seen, the sound of cows and sheep, the sound of children's noise, ..., had also disappeared without a trace! -The whole mountain, was completely submerged in the abyss of loneliness!

A-Fu was a little surprised. He suspected his eyes, suspected his legs, whether he had looked in the wrong direction, walked the wrong road? But when he raised his head again, looked closely at the distant and near mountain peaks, the stone walls and trees attached to the mountain peaks, ... he felt that these were very familiar,亲切, and there was no difference from the one shadow left in his mind. At this time, he was a little flustered, his excited heart, was a little cold. He moved his steps frantically, pushed aside the榛莽, and ran straight into the forest that hid his home. But when he broke in, the terrible scenery that he dared not imagine, appeared in front of him: his home was gone, all the houses, some had completely collapsed, some had been tightly sealed by vines, some had been pierced through the top by wildfires, leaving only four walls standing there! Here, there was no human voice, no barking of dogs, the entire village was filled with a kind of desolate and terrible mist. The mountain birds returning late, were all 高噪着 on the treetops, the dogtail grass growing in the cracks in the walls, was silently nodding there. A-Fu, who had walked across many mountains and rivers with a happy heart, and jumped back, finally fell beside a camellia tree!

Days

— Feier

The days pass slowly, and life is getting shorter and shorter. Watching the calendar being torn off page by page, the ruthless years grind life thinner and thinner. In memory, the childhood years still exist vaguely in the brain, that ignorant state of only knowing how to play and not knowing everything, disappears so far away in a flash. Even in adolescence, that wholeheartedly immersed in books, and not knowing the social phenomena of the vast sky containing all things, it still seems like yesterday when I think about it. Unexpectedly, people have crossed many days, and now not only the taste of society and life has been deeply tasted, the spirit is no longer as innocent and lively as it used to be, and the body has obviously been exhausted, not as strong as in adolescence.

People are sometimes really funny and ridiculous; when bored, they look forward to the early passage of days, but when the days have passed, and they recall the sweet past, they are afraid of the coming of the future. The so-called time is inherently rigid with a certain limit, but due to human affairs, it produces the feelings of love or hatred. It is a deep understanding of this principle that says that the value of time changes with human affairs.

I don't know how the days feel to others. For me, the days are very lovely. Often in the midst of busyness, when I see the events to be dealt with still piled up in stacks, I often curse the fast passage of days, and I always remember those events to be dealt with in my heart. Although sometimes my mood will also fall into loneliness and boredom, and I look forward to the early passage of days, but when I struggle with my limp body, try hard to cheer up, and spend time on various favorite careers, the days feel lovely again, and I hope that they can crawl slowly like ants.

Now, when adolescence has passed and old age has not yet arrived, I feel especially precious for the days. The past is already past, and the future has not yet arrived. For the present, I should use this energetic age to engage in my favorite career, so that the days will not be wasted, that is the reason why I cherish my days. Although I don't quite admire the proverb: "If you don't work hard when you are young and strong, you will only grieve when you are old," but I think it is pitiful and tragic if a person cannot make good use of the days to fulfill his wishes or satisfy his upward hobbies.

Unfortunately, people's days often cannot be controlled by people: Heaven has made it necessary for people to spend most of their energy to obtain food to maintain their lives, and the complexity of human affairs often pulls people out of the circle of making good use of the days and turns them to the garbage heap of waste. Human life is short, and the days and the energy of the human body are extremely limited, then although I want to cherish the days, the days are not willing to be cherished by me. Then what is there to say?

In these times, I have a deeper feeling for the days: watching my beard grow longer and denser day by day, but the career I am doing has not yet achieved any results that can be seen. On the other hand, the disputes of human affairs are becoming more and more complicated, almost forcing me into the limit of not being able to freely use my time. This blow can certainly stimulate me to move forward on my way on the one hand, but on the other hand, the consumption of energy is really frightening. I imagine that if one day my energy is exhausted to the extreme and makes me limp and weak, then career will only become a dream for me, the sense of disillusionment at that time must be very deep, and I can't help but curse the un

Page 21

feeling days!

Days, extinguish the grand ambitions of the world, and also achieve the meritorious deeds and greatness of the world, what will it create me into?

Drought

— Jieren

When a burst of rapid ringing of the bell shook the space, the people hiding in each small room were whipped as if, and walked out one by one, and gathered together in the market. The entire market suddenly became闹 　哄, arbitrary laughter,杂然充塞 in every corner.

Following the ring of the bell, after another three or five minutes, the clock struck a few times, and the members of the institute, wearing uniforms, walked onto the stage one by one in the ringing of the bell. The words "Opening Market", "June Term", "Opening" and other words were successively turned out on the stage, and the human voice seemed to be slightly suppressed. But when the finger of the auctioneer standing in the center of the stage began to gesture in the air, the people under the stage immediately rioted again. "Two and a half points", "Two points seven and a half points", "Pull, pull", "Pull, pull", you shout, he shouts, shouting straight from the throat. At the same time, dozens of hands stretched out, the air was very tense, and each face showed a panicked look as if facing a great enemy.

The auctioneer's eyes stared at the stage, his fingers constantly making various gestures in the air, while拍板 on the table, his mouth quickly念着:

No. 18 No. 20 two thousand, No. 25 No. 31 three thousand, ...

The market is rising step by step!

Still want to rise! Foreign wheat is also more than one元多.

The rain does not fall, and the旱要成, five or six角行情 is not希奇!

Almost as same as last year!

Shouren夹在人群中, is out走出塲口, from behind suddenly have person向就撞,回过头一看, is twenty-one号的小李, Little Li is like just small sparrow, 跳跳蹤蹤, 没有一刻安定, closing 之后不是拉谁谈女人,便是找人打架. He向守仁扮扮鬼脸,笑嘻嘻的说:

Rotten big piece head,挑你不死, want treat!

Shouren Although is a胖子,却最恨人叫他"大块头", 因为这显然太不恭敬了. But today Little Li called him "大块头" he non only not气,反而会心的向他笑了笑,管他走到自己的房间去.

一回到房间里,守仁便倒在沙发中,昨夜马将叉得太晏, 刚才又在市塲里嘶喊一阵, 是使他很感到疲倦的. He闭起目,想养一会神,但是他的神经却不让他安静, 想想今天的市面,"自开盘"后就逐步的涨上去, 這樣子, 不要又同去年一样了吗? 蓦地里, 回忆唤醒了他, 去年也是这样呀! 不过去年是眼睁睁的让它白过去, 今年可不能轻放过, 也得学一次乖呀! 前天报上登着, 有几处地方已在闹旱灾, 无论如何, 照這樣子旱象是酿成, 看看天, 太阳血红的, 不要说雨, 恐怕要比去年还要旱得利害吧!

哈,旱象准成了!

Outside the Iron Grate Window

— Li Ang

Two or three months ago, when I passed by here, the house was being renovated. In the warm air flowing with the fragrance of peach blossoms, the masons, carpenters, and apprentice workers were humming folk songs and working busily. Every day, twice in the morning and afternoon, I would always stand there blankly, watching them打地桩. Erecting steel bars,澆氏敏士,砌石块,铺钢板. The child machine喷 angry吐 black coal smoke, "轟隆隆,豁啦啦……" constantly叫着, like a violent drunkard, hate命往 down wooden poles several丈长 into the ground, the soil经 this番倾轧, began伸张各个方面的势力而震动附近一带的房屋.

The ground work完, the walls一天一天的加高, red 色的磗块,灰色的传块,又阔又厚,年紀小的童工搬不上 four or five块便哼　着移不不开步子了. Ordinary居屋 is not need 这样坚实的砖块的, factory house? Not see烟囱和风筒.堆栈? Not配里面有许多墙壁… I put this疑问保持着,等事实来解决.每天,依然有两次,痴呆呆的站着,看许多泥水匠把墙垣向上建……高,高,高,像一堵城堡.

The wall工稈 successful, the climate already is early summer, hot烈的陽光射照着紅色灰色的墙砖和乌黑发亮的屋顶, 里面 the arrangement is not see, I想不会考究,因为从来没有看考究的材料运进除掉自来永管, 电綫,粗糙的铁条以外. There were window holes on the wall, but they were opened so high, and, also, the blacksmith began to install iron gates in each window hole. I have always doubt what is inside? Once asked a瘦猴子般 的铁匠, he却蹲得高高的,带着讨厌的神色俯首望我一眼, I very识相地走了,the ridge似乎出冷汉.

Connected to electricity, iron window inside, from the darkness透出 a few points发黄的柔弱的灯光, also那样的稀少, like烏雲層層浮于天空的夜晚, 偶尔从云隙里见到一二颗星粒般的. My this颗探求奇迹的心始终叫我留意这座坚牢的屋子的进展. But, that row装铁栅的窗口又装上铁皮罩子了,留一个空口向天空,空口四沿又镶上钢刺,锐利得惊心, 这是防范的设置呵! I 从此认识了这座屋子的威严.

My料想: 铁窗栅里面一定黑暗得不成世界了,难道将来住这屋子的人不喜欢光明?人类是不习　生活在黑暗中的,那么,故意把光明摒隔在外面,而不给予人们享受,总不能不算为是一种　　吧?

Isn't it, no matter that wall有多么厚,终只是一墙的阻隔罢了. The daily sun, the daily moonlight, the daily清快的 wind and naturally flowing气息会降临到铁栅窗外.

The iron栅窗外更替着四季的气候和景色.漂流着孩子的笑,妇女的笑,一切活跃的聲音, 和悅的聲音. They have iron栅窗里的人虽有眼睛却看不见季节的脸,虽有耳朶却听不见自然的欢声. They are being restricted to their world 过着同一本日历上的光阴. Today I walk through here,见红墙脚下已生了几颗靑草,沾着雨露,欣欣向荣, 这在铁栅窗一里是不会有的吧! I瞪着忧愁的眼睛望着地上.、

Ballad Singing

Huang Yuanding Opening Performance

East Land (640) 2:15 PM to 3:00 PM

"Dream of the Red Chamber: Lament of Xiangfei"

A life adrift, devoid of joy, Miss Lin murmurs to herself beneath the silk gauze window. Oriole, having received Bao Yu's instructions, comes to deliver a precious gift and calls out from within. Zijuan, hearing this, rushes to greet her, welcoming her into the Xiaoxiang Pavilion with smiles and words of cheer. Oriole says it's just a small token, expressing his sentiments, a local product from the South for Miss Lin. Soon, Oriole is seen returning to the inner chamber, while the maiden sits in a daze, her brows furrowed. This is all because seeing the gift stirs up memories of her homeland, and now she no longer resides in Jiangdu but in the capital. Ill-fated beauty, Heaven is too cruel. How painful it is that her parents passed away so early. Her uncles and aunts, closest relatives, have all left this world, and even her siblings are gone. She can only rely on her uncle's family to live, and this kind of daily life is like enduring suffering. Who would specially come to the capital to visit her, bringing some products from Yangzhou for her? Thinking of this, her heart breaks, and she wishes she could end this life instantly. The clever Zijuan quickly tries to comfort her, her words flowing like a waterfall, saying, "My lady, your body is usually so delicate. Since taking medicine, it has been very effective. It's not good to be worried, depressed, and keep it bottled up in your heart. My lady, Oriole brought you something from the South. You should be grateful for Miss Xue's deep affection. My lady, the master and mistress both pity you, constantly caring for you and inviting doctors. You must cherish your precious body and not let excessive worry lead to illness. My lady, opening your heart is the most important thing. In the future, you will surely have good fortune." Miss Lin doesn't believe these good words and is filled with sorrow. Fortunately, Master Bao Yu comes to comfort the beauty in person, and she then turns her frown into a smile.

"Modern Youth"

Broadcasting News

The Shipping Broadcasting Station attached to the Shipping Club has now increased its power to 150 watts and broadcasts famous programs every week. This week (the 6th), from 8:45 PM to 9:45 PM, we have specially invited Ms. Xu Lai and Zhang Suzhen to broadcast famous songs. Listeners from all walks of life are kindly requested to pay attention.

Movie News

"Metropolitan Landscape" - Essence Record

Life in the metropolis is like the scenery in a kaleidoscope, colorful and ever-changing, unfolding scene after scene every day. We, who live within it, rarely get a complete picture due to various reasons. The play "Metropolitan Landscape," written and directed by artist Yuan Muzhi, gathers many essences of the metropolis into one, including the old goods stalls that hide filth, the ever-changing stock exchanges, the pawnbrokers who exploit profits, the disguised gambling of candy peddlers, and the bookstores that promote culture. As for the pathological aspects of the metropolis, like the patients groaning in the beds of sanatoriums, the emaciated starving people in the slums, all kinds of shapes and colors, Wu Yin Xian uses his camera to shake out the deformed monsters of the metropolis.

Fragments of "The Jade Horse"

In Xu Xinfu's "The Jade Horse," there is a scene of a morphine production factory, the set design of which took great effort. The props used are especially complex. For the item of Chu medicine bottles alone, thousands of medicine bottles were purchased from glass bottle manufacturers.

The old woman, Gong Jianong, plays a villain selling drugs in "The Jade Horse." Wang Zhenxin plays a detective squad leader. Yan Yuexian plays a shrewd and capable socialite. Between them, there is also a tragicomedy of a love triangle.

Sun Min and Gu Lanjun are siblings here. Sun Min is a young master who lives day to day in a daze, while Lanjun is a smart, capable, and sensible girl.

The opening scene of "The Jade Horse" is a cartoon. In the picture, there is a ferocious demonic shadow. On the right side of the black demonic shadow, there are many demonic flames, their light blazing. On the left side, there are many people who have not been poisoned. The demonic shadow jumps, making seductive gestures. Then, many people walk past the demonic shadow and all become weak and powerless. Suddenly, an electric light flashes and there is a thunderclap. The black demonic shadow immediately flees, and gradually an anti-drug order appears. This very meaningful cartoon is concise and to the point, expressing the main theme of the play even more clearly.

The ending of "The Jade Horse" is that the drug production factory is busted, Yan Yuexian is killed by stray bullets, Gong Jianong is arrested, and the owner of the drug trafficking business is also killed, which makes the audience clap their hands with joy.

The directorial techniques of "The Jade Horse" show that every aspect has been deeply considered and carefully planned. The actors of "The Jade Horse" all fit their roles perfectly, performing with competence and pleasure. The settings of "The Jade Horse" are all magnificent and splendid, novel and worth seeing.

Everyone Flocking to See "Triumphal Song"

According to general film distributors, as long as it is a film directed by Bu Wancang, there is no need to see a sample film, and it can be booked in advance. The reason for this is of course due to the good results Bu Wancang has achieved over the years. Looking at his direction of the film "Humanity," wherever it goes, everyone flocks to see it, which makes film distributors tremble with excitement.

Recently, the tragic and tortuous plot of Bu Wancang's "Triumphal Song" can truly be called an unparalleled masterpiece. Moreover, with early disaster as the background, it can also arouse the sympathy of the people of the country. In particular, Bu Wancang's hard work on this film is astonishing. Every hour, the composition is meticulously studied, and the facilities are all novel and powerful. As for the acting being divine, that goes without saying.

"Triumphal Song" is two-thirds completed. Inquiry letters from theaters everywhere have already poured in. It was once heard that a certain film distributor said, "The beginning of the year is not good, but I still have a glimmer of hope, namely Bu Wancang's 'Triumphal Song.'" The phrase "In the future, everyone will flock to see 'Triumphal Song'" can truly be a portrait of Bu Wancang.

Publishing World

The "Shadow Dance News Weekly," the inaugural issue is scheduled to be published on July 7. In addition to the creations of Hu Ping and Yuan Meiyun, the content is rich in humor and satirical materials. The cover is exquisitely printed on colored copperplate paper, with both pictures and text. It is sold separately for five cents per issue. As a special offer for subscribers, the annual subscription is only two yuan during the special offer period. Please contact Mr. Ye Yifang at Yihua Film Company, Jin Situ Temple, Kang Nao Road.

The special edition of "Electric Sound Movie Pictorial Weekly," Volume 4, Number 27, was published today. The text includes dozens of articles such as "Deteriorating Relationship between Yuan Meiyun and Yihua Authorities," "Diao Banhua's Love Loss Experience," and "Hu Ping Prepares to Be a Bride," "Hu Die's Father Does Not Eat Bran." There are dozens of recent photos of male and female movie stars in the copper pictures. Each issue sells for one dime (this issue). Please send a letter with one dime for postage to Sanhe Publishing House, No. 54 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, and the price will not be increased.

The "Entertainment Weekly" "Inaugural Issue" was published today. The publication combines the "Broadcasting Weekly," "Movie Weekly," "Music Weekly," "Sports Weekly," "Song and Dance Weekly," "Drama Weekly," and "Literary and Art Weekly" into one. The entire book is a large 16mo volume, 32 pages thick, and sells for only five cents per issue. Please send a letter with five cents for postage to Entertainment Weekly, New Number 138 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, and we will be happy to serve you. The annual subscription is five yuan, and five months is one yuan. The publisher of the newspaper is Bao Dejun, and the editor is Liang Tongyun.
